{{Journal entry|
You brought simple cloth trousers with you from the mainland. They barely qualify as armour, but they’re better than no armour at all. 

These clothes have seen you across the oceans, keeping you warm in the cold sea breeze. Now starched with sea salt and weathered by labouring away on the ship deck, these clothes are a testament to how far you’ve come. This is the furthest you’ve ever been from home, and perhaps it’s a chance to craft a new one.  
}}

The expedition offered you a chance away from all your troubles. An opportunity to escape the cruel hand that fate has dealt you. These clothes once represented everything you ever lost, but now they represent the threadbare start of a new beginning.

Prized for its lightweight and nimble nature, linen armour finds favour among apprentice wizards and those who value agility. Composed of layered cloth, it forms a rudimentary defence capable of withstanding minor assaults. 

In the third age, apprentice wizards wore this armour as they practised basic spells. The more senior, blue-robed wizards guided them in their practice and taught them basic enchantments that helped them resist low-level spells and curses. 

The creation of these robes was a sacred duty entrusted to the young acolytes of the faith. It was a testament to their devotion and a means of assisting others in their service to Saradomin.

Prized for its lightweight and nimble nature, linen armour finds favour among apprentice wizards and those who value agility. Composed of layered cloth, it forms a rudimentary defence capable of withstanding minor assaults. 

This simple armour would remain popular with apprentice wizards long into the third age, falling out of fashion only when faced with something more dangerous than a goblin.

The beastmen further north of Brynmoor used weapons far more vicious than a goblin might wield. They tore through linen armour as if it were nothing, and the diminished enchantments of the acolytes did nothing to shield the blows.

Apprentice wizards died in droves, and the armour fell out of favour.

|mat2 = Rune Essence
|mat2qty = 8
|output1 = Apprentice Robe

===Recipe tree===
{{Crafting Tree|Apprentice Robe}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
Prized for its lightweight and nimble nature, linen armour finds favour among apprentice wizards and those who value agility. Composed of layered cloth, it forms a rudimentary defence capable of withstanding minor assaults. 

At first, acolytes would spend time at the wizard’s tower to learn about the magic the armour would protect the wearer against. It was common for young priestly acolytes to become enamoured with the mysterious life of the apprentice wizards. They would see them hurling spells with skill and panache, making their lives of quiet contemplation seem awfully dull in response. Many young acolytes would make linen armour for themselves, practising spellcasting in secret.

The priests soon discovered their numbers dwindling, while the wizard’s guild gained more members. So, the decree was given that robes were to be crafted in silent contemplation, far away from those who would later wear them. This would keep fewer acolytes from being lured away, but the defensive prowess of the armour diminished in return.

The high priests considered this a reasonable exchange.
}}

===== User:RSDWArchive/Armour/Bag Of Noggin =====
{{Infobox Item
|name = Bag Of Noggin
|image = Bag Of Noggin.png

}}
'''Bag Of Noggin''' is an armour item.

==Stats==
{{Infobox Armour
|power = 1
|durability = 500
|meleedefence = 1
|rangeddefence = 1
|magicdefence = 1
}}

==Recipe==
{{Recipe
|facility = Crafting Table
|skill = Artisan
|skillxp = 40
|mat1 = Goblin Pack
|mat1qty = 1
|output1 = Bag Of Noggin
}}

===Recipe tree===
{{Crafting Tree|Bag Of Noggin}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
Noggin was never the best looker in Ashenfall, or so others claimed. He lived his life ashamed of his appearance and wore a sad-looking sack across his face so that none would fall ill from his hideous features.

He found himself an outcast. Mocked and jeered at by the locals of Bramblemead, so he hid himself away in the forests, but kept wearing the sack.

One day, while he was standing in a field scaring birds away, just for the fun, he met a lost villager who had wandered too far. She was frightened, at first, and fearful of the strange figure with a face of itchy cloth, but as they talked and laughed together that fear fell away.

In time, they would grow closer with one another. Developing feelings that Noggin never believed he would feel. On the day they were to be wed, Noggin finally let her see the face beneath the sackcloth, but there was no face to be found.

Instead, when the sack was removed, Noggin’s clothes went limp and fell to the floor in a pile and the woman screamed as the silence engulfed her.

Now Noggin’s face appears on scarecrows and training dummy’s all across Ashenfall, and on cold, dark nights, you could swear they are watching.
}}

<!-- Generated by generate_armour_pages.py -->

===Recipe tree===

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
It's hard not to look at the Black Knight armour and marvel. The Black Knights on Ashenfall have completely different origins from that of the mainland. They have no direct connection to the Kinshra, and are instead evolutions of the Shadow Knights. Two connected but ultimately different factions, yet they converge on similar armours. I suppose that's chaos for you. Stare at it long enough and you spot patterns.

The Black Knights, or Shadow Knights as they were originally known, began life as bodyguards for the Rasmodel family. The Rasmodels were nobility on the mainland, and retained that air of nobility in Ashenfall. They were invaluable to the Children of Shadows, as they could move in higher circles, and higher circles were where the seeds of chaos are best sown. 

The Children of Shadows made the mistake of seeing the Rasmodels as peacocks, preening and insufferable. As time passed, the Rasmodels exerted their influence over the Shadows. They moved into positions of leadership. Every pie had a Rasmodel finger in it, and suddenly the Children and the Rasmodels were synonymous. 

That influence came with demands. The Rasmodels wanted protection. Their scheming in Temple Woods and Bramblemead would lead to the odd fallout, and having bodyguards leant them legitimacy as well as protection. Some of the Children were assigned to the Rasmodel, and a different kind of seed was sown. 
}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
It's hard not to look at the Black Knight armour and marvel. The Black Knights on Ashenfall have completely different origins from that of the mainland. They have no direct connection to the Kinshra, and are instead evolutions of the Shadow Knights. Two connected but ultimately different factions, yet they converge on similar armours. I suppose that's chaos for you. Stare at it long enough and you spot patterns.

Very suddenly, the Rasmodels fell back to the walls of Dowdun Reach. Their cover was blown: the youngest had been caught pouring tincture into the ears of a sleeping bailiff. Their entourage and influence no longer meant anything, and they were forced to live in the keep. A wing was allocated to them, mostly out of fear: the bodyguards were loyal to the Rasmodels, and the Children of Shadows wanted to wake up in the morning.

On the death of the father, the eldest Rasmodel son, Milliburn,  looked to regain some of the family's lost pride. He burrowed himself deep into Dowdun: he was integral to the training of forces; he took charge of the quartermasters. He showed all the hallmarks of a leader, and was duly elected as Master of Dowdun Reach. The Children of Shadows took to calling him 'Lord Rasmodel'. His bodyguards never left his side.  
}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
It's hard not to look at the Black Knight armour and marvel. The Black Knights on Ashenfall have completely different origins from that of the mainland. They have no direct connection to the Kinshra, and are instead evolutions of the Shadow Knights. Two connected but ultimately different factions, yet they converge on similar armours. I suppose that's chaos for you. Stare at it long enough and you spot patterns.

The Children of Shadows learned to be wary of Lord Rasmodel in the mornings. He was cruel before noon, fair in the afternoons, and stern all day. Those who were close to him knew the reasoning: Lord Rasmodel slept poorly, and would complain that his dreams kept him up. He was confused by them: they talked in words that he didn't recognise. He found their voices to be dull and interminable, like being locked in a room with a droning aristocrat. 

The dreams made him impatient and quick to bore. His relationship with Alric, Archmage, deteriorated. Rasmodel even suspected that Alric was behind his restless nights. 

One morning, Rasmodel emerged with a different kind of impatience. He was resolved that something had to change. Fellhollow, Imaru and Xikotal were not to be trusted. A new order of knights were to be created, and he was to lead them. At their centre would be his bodyguards, loyal and unquestioning. 

The Shadow Knights were born, and time would harden them into the Black Knights.
}}

===== User:RSDWArchive/Armour/Bloodblight Cape =====
{{Infobox Item
|name = Bloodblight Cape
|image = Bloodblight Cape.png
|type = Armour
|description = A cloak commemorating a dragon's vengeance.
}}
'''Bloodblight Cape''' is an armour item.

==Stats==
{{Infobox Armour
|meleedefence = 2
|rangeddefence = 2
|magicdefence = 2
}}

==Recipe==
{{Recipe
|facility = Crafting Table
|skill = Artisan
|skillxp = 0
|output1 = Bloodblight Cape
}}

===Recipe tree===
{{Crafting Tree|Bloodblight Cape}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
The Bloodblight swamp was once a pleasant place. Golden fields of wheat, rustling in the breeze. Life here was simple yet fulfilling.

Until Velgar took it all away.

He fought the mighty god of war, Bandos, and he should have lost. Dragons are powerful, and Velgar is stronger than most, but even in his most arrogant days he was no match for a god.

Yet, arrogance is not a mortal taint and the war god reeked of it. Bandos cast aside his wards. He refused to don his armour. The god pressed into the lair of the great dragon, and tried to wrestle him to the grave.

He nearly succeeded. Bandos wrapped his arms around the dragon’s serpentine neck and dug his fingernails beneath the scales. Velgar, in his writhing fury, called down a poison-filled rock from the heavens and cast it at Bandos, striking him in the temple. As the god reeled, he released Velgar, allowing the dragon to breathe a jet of anima-infused poison, at the unsteady god. Still wavering from the blow, Bandos breathed in the toxins and felt weakness for the first time in centuries.

A smart tactician, Bandos retreated. Better to face the shame of retreat, than risk the oblivion of death.

In his jubilant rage, Velgar spilled his blood on the once fertile plains, corrupting them with his hate-filled poison. The fields wilted. The crops blackened and then collapsed into venom.

This cloak, is reminder of that blighted day.
}}

<!-- Generated by generate_armour_pages.py -->

===Recipe tree===
{{Crafting Tree|Blue Dragonhide Body}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
Blue dragons are not native to Dowdun Reach, because blue dragons are not native anywhere. They are creations of the dragonkin, and this particular strain is Lacrussa's work. Lacrussa did not consider them failures, but she did not consider them successes, either. They were stepping stones: and, as such, she let them rest on Dowdun Reach.

Rasthin changed everything. She came to Avisk with a gift: 'Jas Moksha', in the tongue of the Kin. It was a device that imbued Avisk with the element of air. Avisk accepted the gift politely. Rasthin could have over-powered him with ease. He played supplicant and took the gift, hoping that it wasn't a trap or curse.

That disdain shifted once Avisk realised that the powers were not limited to the material realm. He could move with alacrity, purpose and strength in the minds of others. Minds that were once closed to him blossomed like a flower. He dabbled with ogres, and then moved on to blue dragons.

Within the minds of blue dragons, he found a secret. There was a blockage - a multi-faceted prism - that kept their potential at bay. It redirected their thoughts in wild directions, made them unruly. It seemed that their animalistic nature was a product of mental hindrances, rather than physical. With his new powers, he could solve a problem that had hounded Lacrussa for centuries.
}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
Blue dragons are not native to Dowdun Reach, because blue dragons are not native anywhere. They are creations of the dragonkin, and this particular strain is Lacrussa's work. Lacrussa did not consider them failures, but she did not consider them successes, either. They were stepping stones: and, as such, she let them rest on Dowdun Reach.

Avisk maneuvered the multi-faceted prism within the blue dragon's mind. He observed it using his mastery of air, but no permutation would focus the blue dragon's thoughts, no orientation would align the chaos. He resolved to break parts of that giant stone, but its power was diminished with each snap and shatter. He crumpled to the floor of the blue dragon's mind-space in frustration. 

The breakthrough was borne from that frustration. Just as he would move into the consciousness of a living being, he moved into the consciousness of the stone. Perhaps he forgot where he was. Against all his expectations, he was able to step into the stone itself, as if it itself had a consciousness. There was a second layer to the blue dragon's mind.

It is impossible to comprehend what Avisk saw there. But he was forever changed. He no longer cared for healing the blue dragons of their crystalline blockage, of restoring them to sapient thought. Instead, he wished to recreate the prism, the crystal, in the corporeal world. 
}}

|skillxp = 0

}}

===Recipe tree===
{{Crafting Tree|Bramblemead Cape}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
The heart of Bramblemead village was never really the castle, which came much later to the party. It wasn’t the town hall. It wasn’t the druid huts. It was the windmill. Grain heaped by the village was brought here and milled down into flour. The flour became bread, pastry and batter, turning village meals into something that helped people to live, rather than simply survive.

Food, becomes a banner around which everyone can gather. To break bread with one’s enemy was a way to settle old scores, and forge new connections. More good has been done over the dinner table, than on any throne. Flour, turned Bramblemead from a settlement, into a thriving village.

Now, the windmill lies dormant and still. The foundations warped by the centuries, despite the magic holding the rot at bay in the ancient timber, and the stone cracking from time. When humanity fell, it was rats and goblins that claimed the heart of the village, though they had no use for the swirling sails.

To the goblins it was a place where food could be hidden. Supplies sealed up from rival tribes. For the rats, it was a restaurant full of goblin supplies that were never well sealed.

The sail no longer turns. But, perhaps, in the fullness of time, this village heart might beat again.
}}

On Ashenfall, it was used to show that the old ways could stand beside the new. For a while, in the third age, druids wore pins of copper, and the Saradominist priests wore tin pins. {{Journal entry|
The dragonkin of Ashenfall all reveled in power, gaining elemental mastery from the strange anima of the land. Although their kind tended to ignore magic, in favour of alchemy and science, the dragonkin of Ashenfall enjoyed their time as sorcerer kings.

They were robes that empowered their magic, using alchemical techniques to create cloth that would resist their elemental powers. Fire would not burn so easily, cold would not damage the threads and lightning could be turned aside with a flick of a cloak. Though these techniques are lost to time, the echoes of their powerful resistance remains.

The hood was designed for two purposes. The shadow it cast upon the dragonkin features, made their visage scarier and intimidation easier. Goblins, humans and garou would cower from the reptilian grins that was all they could see in the darkness. The second was to hide their frustration at the foolishness of others, their fellow dragonkin included. Rolling eyes is much easier when no one else can see.

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
The dragonkin of Ashenfall all reveled in power, gaining elemental mastery from the strange anima of the land. Although their kind tended to ignore magic, in favour of alchemy and science, the dragonkin of Ashenfall enjoyed their time as sorcerer kings.

They were robes that empowered their magic, using alchemical techniques to create cloth that would resist their elemental powers. Fire would not burn so easily, cold would not damage the threads and lightning could be turned aside with a flick of a cloak. Though these techniques are lost to time, the echoes of their powerful resistance remains.

Lacrussa was the only dragonkin to resist the alure of magic. She insisted that science was the greater power, capable of almost anything with time and study. Lacrussa wore the robes as an a small act of rebellion, claiming that magic would always be overcome in the end.

Unlike her companions, Lacrussa refused to decorate her robes. She took no joy in precious stones, or shining metals. She refused to embroider designs across the cloak. She did, however, use alchemical techniques to enhance the defensive power of the robes. Something the other dragonkin soon came to copy, proving, in her mind, the superiority of science.
}}

{{Journal entry|
The dragonkin of Ashenfall all reveled in power, gaining elemental mastery from the strange anima of the land. Although their kind tended to ignore magic, in favour of alchemy and science, the dragonkin of Ashenfall enjoyed their time as sorcerer kings.

They were robes that empowered their magic, using alchemical techniques to create cloth that would resist their elemental powers. Although dragonkin tend to favour form over fashion, they stitched these robes with undeniable regal zeal. They were more elaborate than necessary, more stylish than required, feeding into the egos of their wearers.

Rasthin, it is said, was particularly fond of stitching elaborate filigree into her robes. Made from threads woven with precious metals, and gemstones, her robes would sparkle and glitter as she flew across the realm, and when she brought forward her flames, everyone marveled.

Glittering against the sky, she inspired devotion as much as fear in her subjects.

{{Journal entry|
Brakka’s hubris was a marvel to behold, perhaps more impressive than any monument of his construction. When Rasthin shared with him the elemental power she had wrung from Ashenfall’s mysterious vents, Brakka became a master of the earth itself.

With the power to shape stone and soil, by will alone, Brakka could have created great villages. He could have constructed aqueducts and watermills that could brought Ashenfall into a new, golden age. Instead, he made a tower.

Kuldra, the godeater, crushed him beneath her great claw and feasted on his anima-rich soul. Stealing Brakka’s power for herself.

She gifted Velgar, her most trusted general, with the elemental mastery of the fallen Nodon architect, and, to mock the dragonkin further, Velgar took Brakka’s monument as his new lair.

Now the tower stands for all to see, as a reminder of dragonkin hubris, and rightfully deserves its new moniker; Brakka’s folly.

With it’s scaley hide in his possession he spent weeks fashioning powerful armour from the remains, until he had an outfit that resembled the creature he hunted.

So dressed, he set out towards the great stone circle near Emberwood, knowing that a dragon had recently made it its home. He would slay it, claim its heart and present it to the woman he loved and she would surely agree to be his forever.

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
Hardened leather is a sturdier defence, able to turn away more powerful attacks. Favoured by hunters and rangers, who like the defence it offers without the reduction in mobility brought on by sturdier armour.

During the schism and the inner conflicts between ‘pure’ humans and the Amalgamated, Wild Knights would sneak into the village and rescue persecuted Amalgamated under the dead of night. Their armour was silent enough to allow them to move through the village quietly, and they had enough mobility to make a quick escape if caught.

Those who captured Amalgamated were rarely well-equipped soldiers, and their knives were often turned away by the hardness of the leather. During those dark times, this simple armour saved many lives.  
}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
Hardened leather is a sturdier defence, able to turn away more powerful attacks. Favoured by hunters and rangers, who like the defence it offers without the reduction in mobility brought on by sturdier armour.

In poor weather, particularly rain and cold, the armour would create a distinctive creaking noise. Barely audible for the most part, but in the silence of night it felt like a deafening roar. Wild Knights made up for the sound of their armour, as they crept through the streets to rescue Amalgamated, by using simple spells to distract people.

They called animal spirits, notably crows, ravens and magpies, which would caw angrily at anyone nearby. This would earn the term “dark tidings”, referring to whenever the Wild Knights were seen near town – in reference to the magpie spirits they would summon.  
}}

Hardened leather is a sturdier defence, able to turn away more powerful attacks. Favoured by hunters and rangers, who like the defence it offers without the reduction in mobility brought on by sturdier armour.

Wild Knight hunters would favour this armour when visiting the forests of Brynmoor. Hard leather was sturdy, and the colours blended more easily with the treeline, allowing them to stalk their prey more stealthily.

For those of Amalgamated heritage, the armour was more easily shaped around any inconvenient mutations, and many a ranger would theme their armour to match. Fire-touched amalgamated were poorly suited to the armour, cooking the leather as they went. But those affected by plant-like mutations would enjoy blending leather and leaf.
}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
Blacksmiths everywhere favour iron as a material to forge with. It is strong, durable, and malleable when hot and yet rigid when cool. It has been used to create weapons and unbreakable containers. Yet, it is most popular when turned into protection for those forced to ride into battle.

During the third age, the blacksmiths who travelled with the Saradominist priests brought the technique of iron to the people of Ashenfall. Previously relying on leather, bone and more easily extracted metals, the introduction of iron brought great change to the village's way of life.

They crafted more robust tools, mightier weapons and armour that practically erased the natural fear of heading into the woods. Only the Wild Knights opposed this new material, fearing its sudden popularity would impact the continent's ecosystem.  
}}

Blacksmiths everywhere favour iron as a material to forge with. It is strong, durable, and malleable when hot and yet rigid when cool. It has been used to create weapons and unbreakable containers. Yet, it is most popular when turned into protection for those forced to ride into battle.

The desire for iron was so strong in the village of Bramblemead that they exhausted all the iron deposits in Brynmoor. The Wild Knights cautioned them to look for more sustainable methods. Still, the villagers had become too accustomed to the luxury of iron.

Militia groups began to form to search Ghornfell for the precious metal ore. They marched in large groups, crushing plants beneath their metal heels and destroying whole areas of woodland in search of iron ore.

Their noise and bluster drew the ire of roving Garou, who saw the invasion of their forests as a violation of their treaties. 
}}

Blacksmiths everywhere favour iron as a material to forge with. It is strong, durable, and malleable when hot and yet rigid when cool. It has been used to create weapons and unbreakable containers. Yet, it is most popular when turned into protection for those forced to ride into battle.

From the outset, the search for iron ignited a fierce conflict between the humans and the Garou. Each incursion escalated the tension, pushing both sides perilously close to the brink of war. However, the situation reached a critical juncture when Bandos dispatched an emissary to the villagers of Brynmoor, offering a solution to their Garou predicament.

The Saradominist priests met with emissaries of Bandos and came to an alliance. The humans would claim the mines of Ghornfell, as long as Bandos could claim the head of the Garou goddess, Lougrim.
A win-win, as far as the priests were concerned.

With a distinct aroma, leather armour became very popular with warriors and hunters, as well as a few villagers, but that’s another story. Leather, when properly layered and cured, can turn away both the claws of a beast and the blades of an assailant.

Some craftsmen would create more elaborate armour, trading functionality for impressive style. With the discovery of anima twisted plants that existed in vibrant hues, new dyes were crafted, allowing for colourful and eye-catching armour.
This would prove problematic when attempting to be camouflaged on the hunt. Many a colourful set of armour would be found in tattered shreds in the woods. The owner of the armour lost to the wilds.

{{Crafting Tree|Leather Chaps}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
With a distinct aroma, leather armour became very popular with warriors and hunters, as well as a few villagers, but that’s another story. Leather, when properly layered and cured, can turn away both the claws of a beast and the blades of an assailant.

Brynmoor villagers favoured simpler styles, which were easy to produce and focused on defence. When traversing the wild forests of Ashenfall, they quickly found that more elaborate designs got in the way. It was better to keep things simple so that they might be more easily repaired than to choose style over function.

Still, it was common for villagers to add small adornments to their leather armour to make them stand out. Patches made to resemble animals were common practices, though flowers were also popular.

Gentle perfumes were also favoured to help limit the leather’s distinctive smell.
}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
With a distinct aroma, leather armour became very popular with warriors and hunters, as well as a few villagers, but that’s another story. Leather, when properly layered and cured, can turn away both the claws of a beast and the blades of an assailant.

It takes time and skill to craft leather armour. The material needs to be cured, cut, shaped and then stitched together with more durable material than simple thread. It can be stiff to move and surprisingly heavy, something young villagers would discover on their earliest hunts.

Young hunters would be gifted leather armour by their family as a sign of their adulthood. Good quality leather armour showed great pride in one’s progeny. Many villagers would compete with one another to gift more elaborate armour as if doing so was a symbol to all others that their child was special.
}}

|mat1qty = 6
|mat2 = Rune Essence
|mat2qty = 6
|output1 = Leggings Of Lightness
}}

===Recipe tree===
{{Crafting Tree|Leggings Of Lightness}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
A cousin to the better-known Boots of Lightness, popular on the Gielinor mainland. These leggings were created by Shana, a Bramblemead villager who hated the cold. While the boots were functional, and useful, making it easier to carry things round the village, she always felt the winds chill no matter what she wore.

Her solution was simple. Since enchantment created an excess of energy, at least when she did it – she was never going to become a wizard – she laced the leggings with the lightness charm.

The effect was twofold. Firstly, she could carry things around the town as easily as if she were wearing the boots. Secondly, the enchantment kept her legs nice and warm.

Fortunately, the designs for these leggings improved over the years, removing the overheating problem that Shana had been so fond of. Although she was doubtless less fond of it after her house caught fire.

Progress demands sacrifice.
}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
Would Dowdun Reach be standing without mithril? At the very least, it would be standing elsewhere. And since 'elsewhere' would put it in the path of dragons, the Withering and Saradominists at various points on Ashenfall's timeline, you would have to surmise that no, Dowdun Reach would not exist.

The Children Of Shadows were once little more than a disaffected rabble. They gathered with the purpose of plotting against Saradominists, but, in truth, most of their time was spent infighting. But even infighting demands a forum, and the Children of Shadows chose Fellhollow Mountains.

The mithril in Fellhollow Mountains (known at the time as Dowdun Mountains) was discovered by a young Zamorakian who wanted to make a raven habitat, something similar to a dovecote. She mined rock and hit a mithril seam. The shimmering metal stunned her, as it has to generations of dwarves. 

She hid her discovery. We do not know why, but we can guess that greed played its part, as it is wont to do. Yet, her discovery was discovered, and the young Zamorakian was killed, left to be picked apart by her ravens. Ravens are an unsentimental bunch.

Mutiny followed, until the Zamorakian chaos subsided. The Children of Shadows now had mithril, a metal that was desired by many. And desire is such a wonderful tool for sowing discontent.
}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
Would Dowdun Reach be standing without mithril? At the very least, it would be standing elsewhere. And since 'elsewhere' would put it in the path of dragons, the Withering and Saradominists at various points on Ashenfall's timeline, you would have to surmise that no, Dowdun Reach would not exist.

The Children of Shadows were no miners, so the extraction of mithril from the mountain was a slow process. Goblins were forcibly employed at the cost of a little food.

Among the order, however, the Children of Shadows had some smiths. These smiths lived dual lives: forging deliberately dull weapons to arm the Saradominists in Bramblemead, and scratching together time for pilgrimages to the Dowdun Mountains. There, they would deliver hardy weapons and armour in the name of Zamorak. 

Making mithril armour and weapons was not permitted, however. To do so would cheapen the metal, to make it seem widespread. Mithril, it was determined, would be a metal of bribery. It would only cross palms, not swords. By keeping it desirable in this way, the Children of Shadows could control its value, and that value would remain high. Only then could they lobby those who would further Zamorak's goals.

How innocent it all sounds now. Mithril is far from rare nowadays, and seams have been found beyond Dowdun Reach. Mithril is just another metal for blacksmiths to dally with. It is no longer a death sentence to make a dagger from it.
}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
Would Dowdun Reach be standing without mithril? At the very least, it would be standing elsewhere. And since 'elsewhere' would put it in the path of dragons, the Withering and Saradominists at various points on Ashenfall's timeline, you would have to surmise that no, Dowdun Reach would not exist.

There was a time, before the Withering, when a choice was made. The Children of Shadows became paranoid about the prospect of attack and betrayal. It did not seem to matter that they were guarded by dragons who manufactured peace. Dark whispers moved them to act.

Their lord, a man by the name of Rasmodel, prepared an edict whereby a faction would form. This would be the Shadow Knights, and the knights would enforce the will of Rasmodel. 

An aspiring knight needs weapons and armour, which led to Rasmodel's choice. Were the knights to wear mithril, the metal that now freely flowed from the mines of Dowdun? It was strong enough, but mithril's value was in its perceived rarity. Or were they to import a different metal, one that would be costly and awkward to source - particularly for a force that wished to remain inconspicuous?

In the end, the choice was made for Rasmodel. The dragon, Xikotal, had a gift. In one claw, he had coal, in the other iron. He wanted to help the Zamorakians, to bring them an offering that might soften their determination to isolate. In the dragon's optimism, the gift would bring the Zamorakians into the wider Fellhollow community. 

Rasmodel had his steel. He could outfit his new order. With the misguided dragon's help, he had his knights. They would ensure the rest of Fellhollow would keep their distance.
}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
A long-held frustration of the Zamorakian magi, the magical sect of the Children of Shadows, was that Zamorak never came to them. At no point did Zamorak ever set foot on the shores of Ashenfall. This fact is key to understanding the resentful mentality of the shadow mage: they feel a constant undercurrent of abandonment. It also explains why they believe that mystic cloth 'came from Zamorak himself'.

The story goes something like this: a Zamorakian apprentice-mage resolved to hang himself. He looked about his room but, so poor was he, he did not have the tools to perform that simple task. His chair could not bear his weight. His bedclothes ripped when he hung from them. He crumpled to the floor in misery. 

In that moment, Zamorak came to him. The mage was awestruck. In Zamorak's hands was fibre that vibrated with magic. It hummed audibly - the mage felt that he could hear chanting from it. When the mage stared at it, the blue shimmered through hues of the rainbow, and then returned to blue.

"Take it, young mage," said Zamorak, and he handed the mystic fibres to the mage. "I will see you in the next life."

In a kind of prophetic panic, the apprentice carried the fibre to an archmage. He relayed how Zamorak had come to him and brought him - alone - this mystical new fibre. He was overjoyed. He wished for the Children of Shadows to have the fabric, and he asked permission to study it.

The apprentice was tried by a council of his peers and stoned to death. His crime was denying the will of Zamorak.

The fibre? The Archmage reverse-engineered its properties, and a new fabric was born.
}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
A long-held frustration of the Zamorakian magi, the magical sect of the Children of Shadows, was that Zamorak never came to them. At no point did Zamorak ever set foot on the shores of Ashenfall. This fact is key to understanding the resentful mentality of the shadow mage: they feel a constant undercurrent of abandonment. It also explains why they believe that mystic cloth 'came from Zamorak himself'.

As mystic cloth became more available at Dowdun Reach, Lord Rasmodel made the decision to allow its trade. The trade partners would be carefully chosen - no Saradominists, obviously. It led to the first interactions between the Children of Shadows and an offshoot of the Garou. They showed no animosity to the Children; more a kind of unbridled curiousity. A friendship, of sorts, grew between Rasmodel and their merchants.

Over the span of that friendship, Rasmodel learned about their affinity to the moon, and their need to remain untethered, nomadic. He did not pry at their religion, but wondered whether this offshoot shared the same god as their counterparts.

It frustrated Rasmodel that he could not infiltrate the Moon Garou, as he did with all other civilisations: he had no one in the Reach with the physiology. So, he resolved to meet with Alric, something he deemed a last resort. 

Alric suggested something interesting. He could not change the appearance of a human to resemble the Garou: that was beyond his capabilities. But the mystic cloth: within that fabric was an opportunity. The material was known to hum, to resonate. But, like a parrot, it could also retain resonance and repeat it. With work, the mystic cloth could surveil the Moon Garou.

Perhaps Rasmodel could infiltrate them after all. 
}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
A long-held frustration of the Zamorakian magi, the magical sect of the Children of Shadows, was that Zamorak never came to them. At no point did Zamorak ever set foot on the shores of Ashenfall. This fact is key to understanding the resentful mentality of the shadow mage: they feel a constant undercurrent of abandonment. It also explains why they believe that mystic cloth 'came from Zamorak himself'.

Mystic cloth was only for use by the Archmage and his council. It was not only a sign of standing within Dowdun Reach; it was a sign that you should probably get on with your work. If you heard the hum of mystic cloth behind you, you had better not be doing something untoward.

The role of mystic cloth changed when Archmage Alric and Lord Rasmodel agreed to meet an attaché of Imaru and Xikotal. It was some cleric from Emberwood, looking to renew an annual trade agreement. 

It was to be a routine meeting, and Alric thought nothing of it. He planned to look at the cleric with disdain and sign the contract provided. But to Alric's scorn, the envoy turned up in mystic cloth. A mystic cloth waistcoat, and a mystic cloth cap, jauntily worn. She was good-natured and jovial, which only made the interaction more painful for Alric.

Alric dared not look at Rasmodel, but he knew that there would be a smirk on that smug face. Alric burned the contract and blasted the envoy off the top of Dowdun Reach. The contract would have to wait.

From that point on, mystic cloth was not reserved for the greatest magi. It was free for any common magi to wear. Alric resolved to wear a different cloth.
}}

{{Journal entry|
Although the name may be sinister, the robes and the people who wear them are not automatically evil. 

The first set of dark mage robes were so named because the technique to craft them required cloth that had been dyed by a unique alchemical mixture. As the years passed and Guthix introduced runes, the mixture was replaced with subtle enchantments, though the appearance was kept the same for tradition’s sake. 

Naturally, many practitioners of magic preferred this armour because of its darker aesthetic. Indeed, many rogue “dark wizards” would don this armour and use magic to engage in sinister undertakings, earning this armour’s moniker a more sinister meaning. 
}}

Although the name may be sinister, the robes and the people who wear them are not automatically evil. 

Brynmoor had a string of so-called “dark wizards.” Most were little more than bandits with a penchant for magic. The guards were enough to deal with most troublemakers, but a small group of them caused real trouble. 
They were members of the “Children of Shadows”, a Zamorakian cult that began to spread through the population. The cult fed on distrust, paranoia and greed, some very human traits. Among this number were three apprentices of the wizard’s guild, who were frustrated that they were not given the promotions they felt they deserved. 

In their quest for power, the ‘Children of Shadows’ stumbled upon ancient vaults, repositories of the dragonkin’s long-forgotten secrets. Here, they discovered the remnants of a forbidden text, a relic of immense power. Driven by their arrogance, they chose to follow its instructions, unaware of the horrors they were about to unleash.

The knights of Saradomin had many names over the years. White Knights. Temple Knights. In Ashenfall they were called Paladins. Brave, and faithful, members of noble families that took up the sword.

They were the second, third and fourth children of Brynmoor’s “nobility” – a title given to those families that were most loyal to the priesthood, and the most obedient were raised the highest.

The chest piece was especially well made. Blacksmiths would take extra special care to make sure that the process went smoothly, as nothing but perfection would withstand inspection. It made forgery practically impossible, or at the very least, far too expensive to work.

It is said that the paladins were capable of working miracles in battle. Rumour held that the power of Saradomin flowed through them, and helped them to smite all who stood against the church.
}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
During the final years of Bramblemead corruption had run rampant. Nobles took more than their share and the priests who watched over them turned a blind eye in exchange for their own share of glittering coin. Those who did not possess noble blood, found that their lives became harder, their earnings became smaller and joy became a much more fleeting feeling than it had done before.

One woman decided to change that. She would attack trader caravans marked with goods for the castle, taking from their purses of coin. Tax collectors would also feel the sting of her arrows, surrendering their wealth to the woman clad in green. She was given the name Nightingale, because of the whistling noise her arrows made as they flew through the air, an almost musical tone that sent fear through her targets.

Villagers would then wake in the morning following an attack, to find purses of coin in flowerboxes, window shelves, or resting neatly under the fattest, laziest, cats.
}}

{{Journal entry|
It was on a cold winter night, that Nightingale and Moragrin finally met. The assassin had given up on interrogating the villagers and worked instead to lay a trap for the highwaywoman. A caravan, loaded with gold, made its way from village to castle under the cover of night, and Nightingale arrived to claim her bounty.

It was a short, but brutal battle. Arrows whistled through the air, making music like an orchestra. Daggers glinted in the moonlight, in a dance of death that would have shredded the life of any normal person. But Nightingale and Moragrin were evenly matched, until an errant magpie brought it all to an end.

Confused by the battle, the magpie had woken from its sleep in a mad panic and dived down at the fighting pair. The distraction was just enough for Moragrin’s blade to pierce the Nightingale’s heart and as she pulled her mask from her victim, Moragrin’s world shattered as she saw the moment the life left the eyes of her younger sister.
}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
The Shadow Knights, or Black Knights, as they would come to be known, were mostly melee and ranged fighters. When magic was needed, they would enlist Alric's magi, but that secondment was always short. The melee knights were mostly posted in the grounds, but the ranged knights had a different role: they were stationed around the demon gate.

Archmage Alric came to Lord Rasmodel with a sheet of paper. It was the morning, when the Master of Dowdun was most impatient. 

Alric had been monitoring the Black Knights. He had suspected something for years now, but today he had proof. The sheet was from a ledger, and it accounted for the number of magi casualties since Alric had become Archmage. There were one-hundred and seventeen deaths, and they came from one-hundred and seventeen incidents. There was no single incident where more than one mage died. 

Alric was in a fury, tossing papers and spitting curses. It was proof that the Shadow Knights were deliberately negligent, that they saw the magi as disposable. Lord Rasmodel kept silent, and let the mage rampage.

The orders went out from Lord Rasmodel the next day. All Shadow Knights were to allow two magi to die with each incident. 
}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
The Shadow Knights, or Black Knights, as they would come to be known, were mostly melee and ranged fighters. When magic was needed, they would enlist Alric's magi, but that secondment was always short. The melee knights were mostly posted in the grounds, but the ranged knights had a different role: they were stationed around the demon gate.

Lord Rasmodel's greatest challenge came from within. It did not carry a sword or crossbow. 

The Shadow Knight numbers were dropping. It was impossible to resign from the order - that was written in the charter - but more and more of the knights were falling into madness. If it were physical wounds, Lord Rasmodel could have done something about the epidemic. He could amputate the problem with a single swing of his sword. But his enemy was intangible. 

He decided to visit those on the precipice of madness. Most were unintelligible, but some talked of food not satisfying them anymore. Others called out to the Dreaming Stone like it was their mother, as if it would save them. In many cases, it sounded like the afflicted were arguing with themselves: two enemies unleashing an enmity. 

One of the mindless disquieted Lord Rasmodel more than the others. She was an afflicted soldier that he knew from long ago. She rambled in a voice that mimicked the droning of a bored aristocrat. Lord Rasmodel knew that voice well. He stumbled from the bedside of the soldier and took no other visitors that day.
}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
The Shadow Knights, or Black Knights, as they would come to be known, were mostly melee and ranged fighters. When magic was needed, they would enlist Alric's magi, but that secondment was always short. The melee knights were mostly posted in the grounds, but the ranged knights had a different role: they were stationed around the demon gate.

Lord Rasmodel gave his Black Knights two sets of orders. The first they were free to discuss, and were encouraged to do so. They were there to protect the magi from the demons. Should one break from its bindings, it was to be put down. In an outbreak situation, the Shadow Knights had full jurisdiction and a freedom to kill with impunity.

The second set of orders was not to be discussed, not even in the company of another. There were two salient instructions. 

Instruction 1: The Shadow Knights would allow for the 'Demon's Share'. Should a demon become unruly, one single mage fatality was encouraged before the demon was to be put down. It was like the culling of rabbits. The mage numbers needed to be managed. 

Instruction 2: Should the flow of demons be too much for the magi to control, the Shadow Knights were to collapse the infernal portal. This was the primary directive: the demons and magi were secondary. 
}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
The last hunter in Fellhollow hid in the trees for as long as he could. Beneath him the dead shambled and stumbled and clawed at the bark, yet he remained in the trees safely out of reach.

He fed himself on nuts and berries, stealing form the treasure troves of squirrels and birds, occasionally risking a trip to the ground to hunt a passing animal. He gave up on cooking the meat he hunted, as he could not stay on the ground long enough before the dead rose up to face him, so he tore into the carcasses of deer, sheep and rats, trying his best not to vomit.

He barely noticed when his appetite changed, since he was so used raw flesh and the sickly cold taste of blood pooling in his mouth. So, when the withering began to take him, he hardly noticed.

Sometimes, if you’re quick enough, you may catch a glimpse of a skeleton in the tree branches. Even in death he fears the monsters on the ground.
}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
Poor old Noggin found no peace in death, because even the gods forgot him. When he reached the River Noumenon, there was no guide to usher him through to the Afterlife. No radiant light to beckon him forward into the loving arms of those he'd lost. instead, there was silence and it went on and on. 

Always quiet and forgettable, the universe simply failed to recall him. His name was recorded in no books of the dead. The various creatures that prey on lost souls, never once thought he seemed like a pleasant meal. Instead they did nothing, except to leave him to his wandering, forgotten and alone. 

Then four people went digging where they shouldn't, and that made Noggin mad. Forgettable as he was, he had always made a point of preserving the status quo and to see these four ruffians blindly digging into the soil that had never done anyone a disservice, why that was unforgivable – he couldn't let it stand. So he crept into their camp, and found the treasure they coveted, and secreted himself within the gold and silver, waiting to be found. Found he was, for when they opened the chest they saw no treasure, no jewels, no trinkets of worth – because Noggin had eaten all of them, swallowed the pieces down into the void – they found only a ghostly sackcloth head glaring back at them, with nothing but hate in its eyes. 

This is that piece of sackcloth, and it's not happy to see you. 
}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
Not all druids follow the notion that one must live a life of peaceful coexistence. After all, the animal kingdom is full of conflict and conquest, predator and prey, as well as battles for dominance. Some druids feel, therefore, that to truly emulate nature one must do so fully, including tooth and claw. The problem there is that druids are, by nature, generally on the squishier side and so they needed armour that would protect their vital areas better than their normal robes.

Soon, many druids began wearing these robes made from the bark of Ashenfall trees. The first incarnations were deeply unwieldy, taking on an ungainly and unfashionable cylindrical shape – little more than tree trunks with holes for the arms and legs. They were effective insomuch that attacks rarely got through, but they made it somewhat difficult to retaliate.

Later the wizard Lavernius realises that with a few tweaks, the addition of some elegant fine cloth, one could fashion the splitbark armour into a far more glamorous form. She took to decorating her robes with glittering gemstones and silver filigree, making her stand out from the crowd. An excellent distraction in magical duels, but a terrible spotlight for local thieves.
}}

After all, the animal kingdom is full of conflict and conquest, predator and prey, as well as battles for dominance. Some druids feel, therefore, that to truly emulate nature one must do so fully, including tooth and claw. The problem there is that druids are, by nature, generally on the squishier side and so they needed armour that would protect their vital areas better than their normal robes.

On Ashenfall, it was the druid Pikenmix who first tried to break out of the peace-loving mould. They learned magic that would allow them to hurl flame from their fingertips hoping it might be enough. Yet, as the enemies got too close, she soon learned that she needed stronger defence than her meagre hood would allow.

It was when she was lost in thought, that she found the solution – by walking straight into a tree. Her nose broke in several places and her entire body screamed in pain, yet the tree remained unaffected by her violent interaction.

So it was that she crafted herself a helm made from the very same tree. Partially in revenge, but mostly because she knew how strong the bark could be.

{{Journal entry|
It was late in the development of Fellhollow that the people needed armour. They made do with old hand me down leather and bronze gear, brought with them from Bramblemead, for the most part, because what need was there for armour when you were protected by dragons.

Kuldra would put a stop to that mindset in the end, but it was the Children of Shadows who forged the first steel gear in Fellhollow. One member, in particular, Sadia Vulketra, began to feel that the order lacked the strength it may one day need to defend against the Saradominist forces.

There was no war. No conflict like that in Emberwood, indeed the four major faiths got along rather well with one another. Yet, the history books told Sadia exactly what the priests of Saradomin would do to the worshippers of the god of chaos.

She forged a helm first, with the assistance of one of her many lovers, a blacksmith Amalgamated called Vesk. The first helmet was styled with great curling horns, stained black by the forge’s flames.

Naturally, this style didn’t prove popular with the rest of the village, as they began crafting steel helms of their own, favouring a more simplistic approach, and a feathered plume, to look fancy.

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
It was late in the development of Fellhollow that the people needed armour. They made do with old hand me down leather and bronze gear, brought with them from Bramblemead, for the most part, because what need was there for armour when you were protected by dragons.

Not all members of the Children of Shadows were as paranoid as Sadia, many enjoyed a blending of faiths and would regularly attend the inter-faith meetings held by the elder priests of the different religions. Still, many felt a growing unease building, even in their idyllic village, and so they began to push for the construction of steel armour.

They took the recipes discovered by Vesk and Sadia, and they found cheaper and more efficient blacksmiths to work with. The elaborate designs favoured by Sadia and Vesk, were soon forgotten in favour of much simpler and efficient designs that could be worn by anyone, regardless of faith.

With the abundance of resources in Fellhollow, soon everyone seemed to have a set of steel armour and for many it became an excuse to forge family crests and trim with filigree that set them apart from one another.

They had no idea how necessary these suits of family armour would prove to be.
}}

When Kuldra arrived it was as if the air had grown heavy, pressing down on everyone. A whole village fell silent as the Godeater turned her gaze upon them. As Imaru and Xikotal rose to face her, villagers instinctively ran to don their heirloom steel armour, hoping that they wouldn‘t have to use it, but knowing in their hearts that they would.

War changes everything, even the sky.

The land itself is strewn with the dead. Ancient skeletons of colossal wyrms, the monstrous creations of dragonkin science, lie across the terrain, dead eyes watching over everything. {{Journal entry|
Reinforced leather, with metal plates woven throughout. The plates rest underneath leather coverings, with metal studs to hold them in place, giving the armour its name. Favoured by scouts and hunters for the mixture of agility and defence. 

Dealing with the armour’s distinctive scent soon became a training tool for more dangerous hunters. It taught them to use the wind as a weapon. They would always walk against it, the wind in their faces, meaning that the garou could not smell them coming. When the weather didn’t help them, the Wild mages would cast constant subtle air spells, changing the breeze’s direction.

One wild mage and her friend, a strange boy who wore a wolf’s skull as a mask, got the tactic down to an art. She used strange, sinister magics to enchant bones to maintain air spells, allowing her to precisely control the wind’s direction. She used this to lead the garou into traps, where her ally leapt from the shadows, taking out the unfortunate garou warriors.

While the design of studded leather made it excellent for hunters and invaluable in battles against the garou, it fell short against those who knew its construction. Betrayal is a constant foe, and once the garou war had come to a close, the Wild Knights found themselves at the mercy of it. 

Though there were more dangerous threats, with the dragons that appeared out of nowhere, there were always some that prioritized power and persecution over common sense. Daggers emerged from the shadows and drove between the plates sewn into the leather. The poison on the tips of these blades ended the life of more than a few Wild Knights. 

The assassins called themselves the “Glass Knives” in memory of the serial killer that took the lives of so many Amalgamated. To them, the strangeness of the knights was a greater threat than the dragons, and they were happy to pay the terrible price that their actions would cost.
}}

{{Journal entry|
Reinforced leather, with metal plates woven throughout. The plates rest underneath leather coverings, with metal studs to hold them in place, giving the armour its name. Favoured by scouts and hunters for the mixture of agility and defence. 

Most Wild Knights favoured studded leather armour over the more durable metal plate. Moving through the forests required as much grace as guts, and stealth is always a hunter’s friend. 

When they were brought into the war against the garou, the leather armour proved less popular at first. While durable and agile, leather has a strong and distinctive smell. The garou’s olfactory senses were much stronger than humans were prepared for, capable of tracking down the leathery smell from a disturbing range. Wind magic helped to keep the scent away from them, but it wasn’t enough to eradicate it. 
}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
It is said these swamps are haunted. Those who wander it at night, tell stories of whispering that bubbles up from the fetid water.

There is a coldness to these swamps, that is more than just temperature. It reaches beneath the warmest clothing and presses itself into bone and blood. Heartbeats slow and bravery breaks beneath its touch.

The trees here are old and spiteful, their roots wrapped around the bones of adventurers, villagers, and warriors alike. They care not for goblin, human, or garou, they will strangle the remains of any within their reach.

Occasionally tiny stones will bubble from the surface, black as midnight and cold as the darkest winter night. A villager once tried to craft jewelry from these stones, thinking them beautiful. It took twelve village guard to put an end to her murder spree.

This cape is woven from the fibres of swamp plants, and shields its wearer from the swamp’s whispers. Or so the old wives tales claim.
}}

Enraged, he took his sword and cleaved Saradomin’s symbol from its plinth, causing it to crash to the floor. Filled with guilt, he hid the fallen piece from his sight. His last act was one of blasphemy, but perhaps an act justly performed.

Archers of the Wild Knights were quick, silent and deadly. A joke their more melee focused companions used to raise on those rare occasions that the knights would gather. Drink and company lead to banter and poor jokes, which created much missed laughter that the Wild Knights always enjoyed.

Archer, warrior or mage, the Wild Knights would hurl jibes at once another, without a moment’s thought. Yet, when needed, there was no stronger camaraderie and they would all die for one another.

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
Zamorak never came to Dowdun Reach. Its gates were never graced by the mahjarrat. No general came, or ambassador from the mainland. Even the ZMI failed to send an offshoot to the keep. 

How was that possible? Chaos taught them that, by simple laws of averages, a high-ranking Zamorakian should have stumbled onto their shores. Ashenfall and Dowdun Reach was too much of an opportunity. Greed must have led a Zamorakian highborn here. 

The silence was deafening. Everyone who lived or worked in the keep knew what this meant: Zamorak had barred his inner circle from visiting Ashenfall, likely at pain of death.  How else could Dowdun Reach have been left alone for so long?

But why? Why did Zamorak keep Ashenfall at arm's length? The answers differed, depending on the zeal of the follower. Zamorak feared something on Ashenfall. Zamorak knew that something made it worthless. Zamorak was already here, just without Dowdun's knowing. Zamorak is in all of us.

Remarkably, that mystery only strengthened the beliefs of Dowdun's Zamorakians. By being so contemptible to Zamorak, they were utterly important. They were main characters in Zamorak's performance. 

It suggests another reason why Zamorak might have left Ashenfall alone. Perhaps he wanted to show that nothing - not even his disdain - would soften his people's infatuation. 
}}

{{Journal entry|
It's hard to look at what the Zamorakian Mages have become. They were once a noble order, committed to chaos, demonology and destruction. You would fear to be in their presence, particularly that of their leader, Alric. Now, you fear them for wholly different reasons. The Reach has twisted them into something bestial. 

The downfall was sudden. They would not admit it, but the magi had lost control of their demons. Their reaction was the same as always: to deny and deflect. If you accused the magi of summoning demons outside of sanctioned areas, they would smirk and give a carousel of different answers: you are lying; you are mistaken; you are cowardly; you are to be eaten by demons. 

Something terrible was bound to happen; it was a question of when. An infernal demon materialised during a Shadow Knight training session. The recruits were memorising guard rotations, so only their teacher was armed. It was a massacre. 

Alric and Lord Rasmodel locked themselves in the war room to argue. None were to enter. Only the two of them know what was said - oh, to be a raven, watching - but everyone knows the result. 

The Dreaming Stone, and the allocation of power that came from it, would be managed solely by Lord Rasmodel. The demon portal would have its power rationed.

Alric and his magi had their wings clipped.
}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
It's hard to look at what the Zamorakian Mages have become. They were once a noble order, committed to chaos, demonology and destruction. You would fear to be in their presence, particularly that of their leader, Alric. Now, you fear them for wholly different reasons. The Reach has twisted them into something bestial. 

Before the re-routing of the Dreaming Stone's energy-flows, people weren't exposed to the energy tethers for long. But now that Dowdun Reach was a lattice of Dreaming Stone energy, that changed. The flows ran through people's rooms as they slept. It pulsed and hummed and bled.

People began to change. Dreams became rarities; nightmares the commonplace. People heard whispers in quiet moments. Through lack of both sleep and solace, the magi were frayed at the edges. They would be quick to anger.

Then the infestation came. People fell sick; a great wave moved from the magi wing outwards. The lucky were feverish or comatose, left to die on stretchers. The unlucky carried battles in their heads. Voices warred within them, and they would buckle over in pain as screaming headaches took them. 

The epidemic was so terrible, so consuming, that Lord Rasmodel's actions might be considered understandable. He was desperate, and likely ill himself. 

Lord Rasmodel shattered the Dreaming Stone with his warhammer. It smashed - its shards tossed to the winds. For one glorious moment, the voices stopped. Lord Rasmodel felt peace in that moment. But something worse was unleashed, and the horrors doubled.
}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
It's hard to look at what the Zamorakian Mages have become. They were once a noble order, committed to chaos, demonology and destruction. You would fear to be in their presence, particularly that of their leader, Alric. Now, you fear them for wholly different reasons. The Reach has twisted them into something bestial. 

At first, the changes to Dowdun Reach were positive. By throttling the power from the Dreaming Stone, there were fewer incidents at the demon portal. Demons rarely appeared without being summoned, and those summonings were restricted to the portal room. If the Reach was once a lightning rod for demons, it was now grounded with only the occasional spark.

Alric was never going to accept this new status quo. His faithful began re-routing the power of the Dreaming Stone. Energy tethers from the Dreaming Stone passed through and round residences. The Library, which warded against magical overflows, had its power siphoned. 

Where the Dreaming Stone's energy-flows were once arterial, they were now like capillaries. The energy spread everywhere, a webbing throughout the Reach. And that had consequences. 

Some of those consequences were explosive, sudden. The capillaries would overload, leading to fires and outbreaks. The magi would blame the Shadow Knights for these discharges, since Lord Rasmodel was now steward of the Dreaming Stone. 

Other consequences were less sudden. They barely manifested at all, but their effects were insidious.
}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
Wizards always push themselves too far. They compete academically with anything that moves, insisting on demonstrating their intellectual superior over everyone around them. Their intelligence is a glittering brooch that must be seen by everyone.

Naturally, this sort of mentality causes many a wizard to burn out. Academia creates a sort of stress that could be bottled and weaponised, only to be banned by conventions around the world for its cruelty. Yet, a wizard does it to themselves, pushing and pushing beyond the limits of the human condition.

Inevitably they turn to external solutions, and this particular mixture has pushed many a mage past academic burnout just long enough to get by. Somehow it makes magic flow easier, spells cast stronger than before, and the wizard is capable of feats they might never have achieved before.

They also tell themselves that it lets them get by on only two hours of sleep a night. It does not and it all catches up with them in the end. Wizard burnout can be disturbingly literal.
}}

|mat2qty = 10

===Recipe tree===
{{Crafting Tree|Magical Focus}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
The wizard Mallory was never as good as he had hoped to be. He was proficient in spellcasting and his rote memory was excellent, but the power of his spells always fell a little short. He advanced through the ranks mostly through technicality, but he never quite earned the respect of his peers. 

That was until the day he created the focus. Mallory had always been good at making things. He enjoyed the simpler magic of crafting, and he found you could weave small threads of magic into the construction of something, breathing just a little bit more life and wonder into it than before. True craftsmanship, he believed, carried a little bit of the creator’s soul in it. 

The focus proved this theory and elevated it further. By creating a focus and subconsciously imbuing it with a bit of his essence, it would create a smoother, more fluid, channel of magic through the body, which created spells of greater potency. 

Tragically, after sharing his knowledge with the other wizards, he was murdered by his mentor. Who then took his knowledge and claimed it as his own. Karma is a stern judge, however, and the offending wizard later found himself being swallowed whole and digested by a dragon. 

Just punishment, I’m sure Mallory would agree.  
}}

===== User:RSDWArchive/Consumable/Small Wardstone =====

}}
'''Small Wardstone''' is a consumable item.

==Recipe==
{{Recipe
|facility = Rune Altar
|skill = Runecrafting
|mat1 = Stone
|mat1qty = 1
|mat2 = Rune Essence
|mat2qty = 5
|output1 = Small Wardstone
}}

===Recipe tree===
{{Crafting Tree|Small Wardstone}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
Wardstones are handy tools for anyone working with wards. Armour, when created on an anima-rich continent like Ashenfall, is infused with threads of enchantment that harness natural magic to provide an extra layer of protection for the wearer.

This protection depletes upon use, as the energy within the ward is expended on the effect. But the wardstone can rectify this situation… for a price.

The stone around the wardstone is hollow and more brittle than it seems, and the rune essence is carefully laid within it along with a final ingredient – a drop of the creators own blood. This blood, and the rune essence formation, creates a sort of harmonious connection between the bearer of the wardstone and the stone itself.

When the stone is broken, it activates the rune essence and draws anima in from the nearest pure source – the soul of the user.

Souls are containers of pure anima. They grow over time from experience and adventure, the more the bearer of said soul enriches their life with activity, the stronger the soul. This means that the damage the wardstone creates, whilst not insignificant, is easily repaired through the simple passage of time. Especially on Ashenfall, where merely surviving to the next hour is an adventure.

Wardstones are great in a pinch, but one must be careful not to use too many, less the damage they deal to themselves becomes too great.
}}

==Item sources==
{{Drop sources list|Weak Healing Potion}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
Alchemists have long strived to create potions to rid mankind of all their ills. Normally these potions are regeneratives, that boost the body’s ability to repair itself by drawing in the ambient anima and infusing it into the blood and tissue of the drinker. On the mainland this changes healing from a matter of days, to a matter of hours. On Ashenfall the results are far more pronounced.

The ambient anima of the region is so strong, that wounds heal in moments. Cuts vanish as if they never were, the wounds healing so quickly that even scars cannot form. The weaker potions burn themselves out before they can heal massive injuries, but the results are impressive none the less.
}}

==Products==

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
Used in crafting Poison Arrows or to coat your equipped Melee Weapon with Poison for a short time.

There are times in life where you really want someone to regret ever meeting you. It could be a long-held grudge, it could be on the battlefield, or it could be in a never-ending meeting that could so easily have been an email but has now persisted past your lunchbreak and you had so been looking forward to that sushi… ahem… sorry, where was I? Oh, yes, pain!

Poison is sometimes considered to be a coward’s weapon. Personally, I prefer to think of it as the smart weapon choice, after all, honour is only worth anything if you’re the winner of the battle. A corpse with honour still rots in the dirt. With a blade coated in poison, you can almost guarantee the death of your enemies, all it takes is a single nick and their fate is sealed.

An investment well worth making, if you ask me.
}}

{{Journal entry|
The blade is not just a weapon in the wilds of Ashenfall, it’s a tool. Sometimes it’s the difference between seeing tomorrow and having a very bad today. 

Dwarves have always understood the importance of properly maintaining one’s equipment. They turned the care for their weapons into a ritual of almost religious significance. Blades would be cleaned, serviced and sharpened so that they might cut through deadlier dangers and challenge greater threats. 

The whetstone is a simple device, but one that served as a backbone of this ritual. A smith would learn to gently sharpen the blade to the thinnest edge possible, treating it almost like a competition. They would boast and brag with each other about the sharpness of their blades. 

A popular dwarven myth speaks of the Prime Whetstone, capable of sharpening a blade to the point that no armour or metal could withstand it. Sadly, or perhaps thankfully, no evidence exists to provide any truth to the myth.

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
Little is known about the great necromancer, Abraxus, a fact he finds deeply frustrating. In his youth he sought secrets forbidden to others and he wandered the Whispering Swamps of Brynmoor in search of secrets that others dared not know. The swamp was ancient and haunted, so the legends went, and there was a magic to it that was different to any other part of Ashenfall. He explored vaults, caves and battled goblins in the mists, but never found the power that his youth demanded. Until one day, he found the smoke that promised him the power he so desperately craved. 

From there his history is clouded, obscured just as the mist obscured the swamps. He founded a small order of necromancers in Fellhollow and took advantage of the chaos when the Withering began. He sought to bind the souls of the dead into his service, gaining power just as Imaru gained hers from the consumption of the fallen. 

But Abraxus was no dragon, and so frustratingly mortal. A single hoplite spear is all it took to end his life, he would have been embarrassed if he felt it had mattered. As a spirit he lost a lot of things we take for granted, sensation, corporeality, and many of the emotions that everyone else enjoys. Yet, in exchange, he was given the most precious gift of all – time. Time to contemplate. Time to scheme. Time to think about what really matters, in the grand scheme of it all, and he has found his answer. 

His ring, imbued with his dark power, offers no value to him any more. So he bequeaths it to you. In time, perhaps, it may help you become a mage strong enough to earn his respect. Well, a small fraction of it, at least.  
}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
More and more of the afflicted began talking in the voice that Rasmodel recognised: the voice from his recurring dreams. They were a chorus, moved from the land of dreams to his waking nightmare. Doubt burned in him. Was this epidemic his fault? Was it here for him? 

He couldn't hide his relationship to the epidemic anymore. When he walked past the afflicted, they would move from incoherent to coherent. They would sit up and speak to him. The message was the same: "submit to the Dreaming Stone". There were variations on that theme: use the Dreaming Stone; spread its energy; offer your mind to it.

Lod Rasmodel was resolved. He would never submit. Perhaps therein was the trap. Perhaps it was shrewd psychology to make him destroy the stone. 

But destroy it he did. All it took was a single blow from his warhammer. A great and savage arc. As the crystal shattered and the shards punctured his skin, he felt peace. The voices were silenced. he knelt, bleeding and happy. 

And then the aftershocks came.
}}

{{Journal entry|
Bronze arrows offer greater armour piercing than their non-metallic counterparts. Copper and tin were relatively uncommon in Brynmoor, so using the resources on arrows seemed like a waste of money. One faction of bandits delighted in this premise; their leader, a man known as the Auburn Ocelot—for reasons he would never explain—took great amusement in their use. 

The Auburn Ocelot would laugh as his bandits hurled expensive arrows at the villagers, pilfering coins worth far less than the ammunition used to corral them. To him, it wasn’t about the money but the look of confused terror on their faces and the knowledge that no one could stop him. 

He was above it all. Better than everyone. 

It was a rat that killed him. Not even a giant one. Just a tiny creature carrying a virulent plague. Money could not save him, no matter how much he flaunted it. He was cremated, and his ashes buried in the middle of nowhere so that no one might risk catching the infection that cost his life. 

Now, he’s almost completely forgotten. 
}}

Deadly arrows made deadlier with fire. Each arrow burns with the fury reserved for the most unpleasant parts of Infernus. They sear, they singe, and they melt the flesh, turning their victim into little more than ashes floating away on the wind.

In the days of the great war against the Garou, the priests of Saradomin encouraged the use of these weapons. {{Journal entry|
While heavier than other materials, there’s little argument that a bronze shield is a superior defence to wood and leather materials. The metal turns aside almost any blow, protecting the wielder behind its mass. 

Even the Wild Knights, who usually shunned metal weapons, would don bronze shields into battle. Their philosophy was that a life is worth more than a principle. 

Before the peace treaty with their goddess, Lougrim, the garou would often get into conflict with travelling villagers. They saw the humans as prey, willfully intruding on their land and therefore consenting to be hunted. The humans, of course, saw things differently. 

Garou weapons were powerful and delivered by creatures of unnatural strength. Yet bronze would defend against these attacks, and it gave the garou pause, for they had yet to battle foe with such intriguing technology. Battles that would previously have been a slaughter became skirmishes as the garou tested their might against these new bronze defences. 

This comparative peace did not last long. 
}}

{{Journal entry|
The first bucket on Gielinor was created by Mrs Hyacinth, to help her around the farm. They had buckets back on the human homeworld of Teragard, of course, but she hadn’t brought anything with her from the village Guthix had recruited her from.

The problem was that Mrs Hyacinth had a cow, named the traditional Bessie, that produced an unreasonable amount of manure, and Mrs Hyacinth needed something to help with the clear up.

She used local twigs, at first, weaving together more of a basket than a bucket, and the results were not as watertight as she had hoped. In the end, she meticulously combined strips of wood, tied together with cord, and they were able to withstand even the worst of Bessie’s endeavours.

Now, you too can fill one of these marvelous contraptions with horrifically pungent compost. Spread the smelly stuff across your farming plots and marvel at the health and happiness of your leafy little friends.
