Now, the knight was a large and imposing man -- referred to by his compatriots as the immovable boulder -- and angry as he was, he had no intention of killing Ignatius, so he gave him a simple challenge instead. If Ignatius could knock him down, he’d win the duel, otherwise the Knight would claim victory and see Ignatius punished for his mischiefs.

When Ignatius pulled the crossbow from his robes, the knight was concerned but knew that his armour and shield could stand against them. Yet, when the bolt impacted the knight’s pristine iron armour, he found himself hurled to the floor and the wind knocked out of him.

Gracious in defeat the knight let Ignatius go, only for the wizard to wander into the next person he had wronged.

{{Journal entry|
Stone remembers, wood forgets, iron holds a grudge. So goes the Imcamdo saying. A reference to how much stronger metal weapons were than wood and stone. Still, with magic, this adage can become painfully true.

The first enchanted iron bolts on Ashenfall were crafted by Lina Hesperian, one of the Amalgamated. She had hair that flowered like a waterfall down her spine. Her eyes were crystalline lakes, sparkling in the light, and her smile was as refreshing as any spring. She enchanted the bolts so that they might carry the gift of water, washing away infection for a clean and gentle kill. She made them for the hunters, so that they might claim their quarries with as little suffering as possible.

She met the end that far too many Amalgamated suffered. Alone, frightened, in the cold and the dark of an alley, her blood seeping from the knife wound in her chest. As she gave her last breath, she cursed the world for it’s cruelty, and the iron listened.

Now, each enchanted iron bolt taps into that grudge, inflicting a reminder of her suffering on any that feel the bolt’s sting.
}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
For a short time, a necromancer arrived on Ashenfall. She had found her way here by boat, fleeing pirates who wanted revenge for her misdeeds. Her skills were limited; she could not raise undead legions, but she had a knack for controlling simple fangs and bones. 

She fled into the forests – pirates having found Ashenfall and hunting her down –  where she would unleash fang arrows against her foes in the hope of stopping their chase. It didn’t work. Broken, lost and without hope, she prepared herself for death. 

But death never came for her. 

Instead, a Wild Knight, who wore a mask made from the skull of a wolf, rescued her. He pushed back her assailants and brought her to safety. Their fellowship after that was unbreakable, though no bond of romance flowed between them. She made the arrows, he fired the bow, and together, they feasted on their victories and kept the woods safe from unwanted intrusion. 

Even now, there are signs of their friendship. Hidden across the forest, miniature carvings of a wolf skull and a bat can be found in places that meant something to them.
}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
It is perhaps not surprising that wizard’s made use of magical jewellery as early as possible. Indeed the first few pieces worn on Ashenfall were little more than decoration, and gaudy wizards would attempt to outdo one another with shinier and shinier pieces.

As part of their ever increasing “prank war” wizards began to create jewellery that was enchanted with effects designed to frustrate, or otherwise hinder, the wearer, believing that enchantments in jewellery were little more than silly trinkets. One mage created what she assumed was an auditory illusion, within an amulet, the intention being that when the wearer would try and cast a spell, the jewellery would play an annoying earworm tune, distracting the poor caster.

This did not happen. Something about the threads of magic, the structure of the crystal and the concealing spell that was intended to hide the prank, created something unique. Instead of making it harder to cast spell, the wearers found it easier. Understanding came faster, spells and incantations clearer than before.

What was intended to distract instead focused the wearer, allowing them to concentrate in ways they had never been able to before.
}}

One jeweller, a water-Amalgamated by the name of Lochlan, created an amulet imbued with the communal spirit of the hunters. {{Journal entry|
The first of these weapons was not commissioned for war. Nor was it commissioned for hunting. Instead, this most deadly arrow was created for nothing more than vengeance.

Against a pigeon.

Lord Gawurin was the ruler of Brynmoor, as appointed by the priests of Saradomin. He wore expensive garments of the finest materials, adorned with glittering jewels and gold chain. So, he was most affronted when a single pigeon determined that such a garment was the perfect restroom choice.

The pigeon's audacity was unforgivable. Day after day, Lord Gawurin's garments were defiled by this feathered fiend. His anger grew, fuelling a desire for revenge that consumed him. He commissioned an arrow, a weapon of brutal design, with a single purpose- to make the pigeon suffer.

With a sinister smile, he summoned the most skilled hunter, a woman who had brought down countless foes, and ordered her to end the pigeon's reign of terror.

She stood at the top of the castle, her bow steady, her aim true. The tension in the air was palpable as she prepared to unleash the arrow of vengeance upon the pigeon. The world seemed to hold its breath in anticipation.

She missed. 
}}

{{Journal entry|
A leather shield consists of a thick piece of leather stretched across a wooden frame. Wooden shields are bulky and heavy, making them more unwieldy. In contrast, a leather shield’s relative lightness makes it much easier to move into position. 

Leather shields were popular with the villagers of Bramblemead since the materials were comparatively easy to gather. Young warriors often wielded them as they accompanied druids into the woods, where the druids gathered the herbs for their medicines and rituals. 

The Children of Shadows also enjoyed leather shields, which they decorated with Zamorakian symbols, hoping to intimidate anyone who saw them.

|mat2qty = 1
|output1 = Mithril Barbed Arrow
|output1qty = 33
}}

===Recipe tree===
{{Crafting Tree|Mithril Barbed Arrow}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
Demons dealt with wounds and ailments on their own. There was no such thing as a demon surgeon or sick bay. If wounds were fatal then the demon would die; if wounds were survivable, then survive they did. 

This was an observation of Summoner Flament, who passed it on to Alric, who idly mentioned it to Lord Rasmodel in one of their weekly meetings. As with most information, Lord Rasmodel examined it for opportunities.

If demons sought no help from their wounds - no remedies, no medical assistance - then his knights would carry weapons that took advantage of that fact. Arrows were poisoned, since no demon carried antipoison. And arrows were barbed, as demons would pull them roughly from their hides, rather than remove them carefully. 

It was a small advantage, but Lord Rasmodel took it. As he would often say, "stack opportunities, one on top of the other, and soon you will have an impregnable tower". 
}}

===== User:RSDWArchive/EquipmentOther/Mithril Fire Arrow =====
{{Infobox Item
|name = Mithril Fire Arrow
|image = Mithril Fire Arrow.png
|type = Equipment Other
|description = Burning arrows with tips forged from mithril, coated in fire oil.

|facility = Fletching Bench
|skill = Artisan
|skillxp = 8
|mat1 = Mithril Arrows
|mat1qty = 33
|mat2 = Fire Oil
|mat2qty = 1
|output1 = Mithril Fire Arrow
|output1qty = 33
}}

===Recipe tree===
{{Crafting Tree|Mithril Fire Arrow}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
The Fogger's Gala was one of the few dates that a Black Knight could look forward to. An annual tradition, it would take place on the mistiest day of the year. As soon as low clouds started rolling in, word spread among the knights that it was Gala day.

It was an informal event on the battlements of the keep. There were quivers that represented each of the night's events, and the knights would name their arrows and place them into the quivers of those they wanted to participate in. Arrows were drawn randomly to determine the order. 

Sergeant Blister was on hand with betting. He brought his blackboard, which he seemed to have on-hand when needed, and a week's wages were placed on friends and adversaries. 

The events all revolved around bows and crossbows. The fog made it almost impossible to see anything, so the Gala was a test of both memory and accuracy. One event required the archer to hit hay bales with fire arrows. The hay bales were invisible, so they only had location names to go by - the hut by the waterfall, Skrexis's bed - which meant firing Hail Mary's in the vague direction of their quarry, hoping that it would ignite in the night.

Other events included Pin the Arrow on the Goblin (as you can probably imagine, a noisy goblin ran about in the fog), Farthest Arrow and Alric's Curtains.
}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
The Rasmodels were notorious for their use of poison. When they lived to the south, in Temple Woods and Bramblemead, it was often said that you should cover your cup, mouth and ears around a Rasmodel. One of the family was finally caught red-handed (or green-handed, considering the poison used), and the rumour moved to certainty. They were banished to Dowdun. 

The reputation followed them, and mostly became a gift rather than curse. No-one in Dowdun Reach wanted to cross the Rasmodels for fear of waking up in spasms. 

We say that it was 'mostly' a gift, because of an event between a young Lord Rasmodel and his cousin. Lord Rasmodel claimed that he could shoot an apple from the top of his cousin's head, and promptly did so. He handed one of the resulting apple-halves to his cousin who ate it, and promptly keeled over and died.

It turned out that the arrow used to the cleave the apple was poisoned. Lord Rasmodel claimed that he had been using his father's hunting arrows, and one of them must have been tainted. It seemed entirely plausible.

But there was still doubt. And that doubt grew into a reputation: a reputation that outmatched his own family's. Even at the age of eight, the inhabitants of Dowdun Reach gave Lord Rasmodel a wide berth.
}}

The name is a bit of a misnomer, since this amulet has very little to do with the river Salve. Instead its name refers to the crystal that traditionally sits at the heart. This crystal was first brought to the region by Saradominist priests, some time in the third age. They had harvested it from a cave near the river Salve and found ways to cultivate on Ashenfall’s soil, by utilising the natural magic infusing everything.

Sanctified by faith and magic, this amulet was deadly to the undead, and the dragonkin Lacrussa was fascinated with the properties. She stole the recipe for its creation and hid it within her vault, long before the withering curse spread over Fellhollow. Instead she had delved too deeply in her own experiments and discovered something buried within the earth that would twist and reanimate the dead.

This amulet allowed her to hold the forces back and keep them from overrunning her lab. That was, until, she met her end at Kuldra’s fangs.

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
There are few things as good at shielding you from harm, as a great slab of metal between you and your foe. The steel shield is more durable than its iron kin, capable of resisting greater and more deadly blows.

It was popular among Fellhollow locals, who would play a game that indicated an intelligence shortage among the population. The game consisted of one player being equipped with a crossbow and other players would hide around the area carrying steel shields. The crossbow wielder would then hunt the other players and try and fire a bolt into their shields, marking them as out of the game.

Unsurprisingly the injuries caused by this game were large and common place. Even the death of some of the players wouldn’t cause the activity to be banned. “It’s tradition”, “it’s just good fun”, “hardly anyone gets hurt”, these were the arguments made even as parents grieved the loss of their child from the game.
}}

{{Journal entry|
The stone arrow's weight and durability make it a more popular choice among hunters. The hardness of the tip makes it better at piercing tough animal hides or less durable forms of armour. In the second age, druids considered it a form of cheating, citing that it required a human's ingenuity to create rather than being a gift of nature. 

They seldom complained when the evening meal was served, celebrating the success of the hunt alongside everyone else. 

Even with somewhere as remote as Ashenfall, some humans turned to banditry, and they were very fond of stone arrows. Cheap and easy to produce, they help to kill and threaten anyone who makes the mistake of travelling through bandit-controlled woodland. 

One such bandit, the self-described "bandit king, Otho", would choose only "interesting" stones to turn into arrows. Glittering pebbles that swished through the air. He was nicknamed the "Magpie King" because of his love for shiny pebbles. A moniker he was very unhappy with.

===== User:RSDWArchive/EquipmentOther/Wooden Arrow =====

|type = Equipment Other
|description = A very basic arrow.
|stacklimit = 999
}}
'''Wooden Arrow''' is a equipment other item.

==Recipe==
{{Recipe
|skill = Artisan
|mat1 = Ash Logs
|mat1qty = 2
|mat2 = Feathers
|mat2qty = 1
|output1 = Wooden Arrow
|output1qty = 33
}}

===Recipe tree===
{{Crafting Tree|Wooden Arrow}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
Druids dislike violence but understand its place. The natural world is full of blood, murder and death. The strong consume the weak. Predator against prey. This they understand, though they seldom like it. When they must resort to violence, they choose the simple approach. Man’s strength comes not from their muscles but from their creativity and ingenuity. Just as a wolf has claws, a hunter has a bow. 

When a bow must be drawn, the druids prefer arrows made of simple wood. Gathered twigs and branches, whittled down to sharp points. They see it as the forest giving them the blessing to go on the hunt. Traditionally, feathers are gathered from around the forest floor, taken when dropped or from a bird’s moulting. This keeps the number of arrows low, forcing a hunter to be accurate and precise, lest they run out of chances. 

Thus, death is swift at the hands of a bow, and balance isn’t damaged. This the druids preached to the villagers. 
}}

{{Crafting Tree|Wooden Watering Can}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
Rain is unreliable. It is far too whimsical in when and where it falls. Relying on its good nature is a sure-fire way to court drought, famine and ruin. Because of this, the druids created rainfall you could hold, handheld containers of water that could be summoned when and where it was needed.

Fill one of these up from any water source and you can use it to keep your farming plots nice and moist.
}}

{{Journal entry|
Simple wheat, water, yeast and salt, combined together and incinerated within an oven. A staple across many cultures and species across Gielinor and beyond. The Icyene of Hallow enjoy a flatbread that they can wrap food in, for a meal on the wind. The aviansie of Abbinah, when the limited wheat is available, prefer a thick and sturdy bread, so that each bite lasts longer. Elves enjoy a sourdough, priding themselves on how long they can keep the starter alive.

For the people of Ashenfall, much like their cousins in the mainland, a simple loaf is more than enough.

===== User:RSDWArchive/Food/Roast Dinner =====
{{Infobox Item
|name = Roast Dinner

|description = It's not even Sunday.
|weight = 2.0

}}
'''Roast Dinner''' is a food item.

|mat3qty = 1
|output1 = Roast Dinner
}}

===Recipe tree===
{{Crafting Tree|Roast Dinner}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
Imagine it. You gather around the table, the warm smell of a freshly cooked roast wafts across the room. Your mother places a bowl of roast potatoes, so divinely crisp that you wonder if they’re even real. Your sibling places a tray of freshly cooked vegetables, a kaleidoscope of colourful foods waiting to be consumed. Your father, doggedly sticking to traditional gender roles as if the past is an anchor weighing him down, slices into the roast serving each of you juicy cuts of meat that make your mouth water.

And what are you doing in all of this? Hrmm? Nothing, that’s what! Pull your life together Stanley!

If your name is not Stanley, you can ignore that above message.

Here on Ashenfall you do not have those smiling faces to reflect upon, only the memories elucidated by the roast meat before you. As you tuck in, you’ll recall those moments of happier times, before you got stranded here with nothing.
}}

===== User:RSDWArchive/Other/Black Metal Scraps =====
{{Infobox Item
|name = Black Metal Scraps
|image = Black Metal Scraps.png
|type = Other
|description = Dropped from Black Knights. Can be reforged into black metal at a blast furnace.
|weight = 1.0
|stacklimit = 99
}}
'''Black Metal Scraps''' is a other item.

==Products==
{{Uses material list|Black Metal Scraps}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
Fun fact: black metal is actually steel that has gone through a form of vulcanisation. Demonic or draconic sulphur are used in the process, to slightly different effect. Demonic vulcanisation gives the metal a matte finish, while draconic is more chromatic. 

What you have here is some scraps of black metal. Could be demonic, could be draconic. They're likely off-cuts from the smithing or vulcanisation process, or it's entirely possible that they were bashed off a Black Knight's armour when you boffed them. Regardless, waste-not, want-not. Now you have the material required for some new gear.
}}

{{Journal entry|
You may wonder where the 'cursed' moniker comes from. There is no need to worry: you're not cursed by wearing it, and you're not going to be visited by the three dragons of past, present and future in the night for making it. It has a wildly different etymology. 

The 'cursed' is a tannery thing, you see. Cursed leather is notoriously hard to work and shape. Only the foremost tanners can manipulate it. But even they have a hard time, often exclaiming "cursed leather!" at the top of their lungs.
}}

===Recipe tree===
{{Crafting Tree|Demonic Oil}}

==Products==
{{Uses material list|Demonic Oil}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
Combine corrupt bonemeal and vile ashes and the result is demonic oil. We should be specific about what kind of oil this is: please do no pour it into a frying pan or use it on a squeaky hinge. This is potent oil, as the 'demonic' prefix will attest. It is used for crafting, and solely for crafting.

Now you've got us wondering what would happen if you did actually add it to a frying pan or a squeaky hinge. Obviously, please don't do it. But if you do happen to do it, through an accident or momentary lack of wisdom, could you let us know what happens? 
}}

}}
'''Focused Farming Potion''' is a other item.

==Recipe==
{{Recipe
|facility = Brewing Cauldron
|mat1 = Irit
|mat1qty = 1
|mat2 = Undead Bone
|mat2qty = 1
|mat3 = Glass Vessel
|mat3qty = 1
|output1 = Focused Farming Potion
}}

===Recipe tree===
{{Crafting Tree|Focused Farming Potion}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
A common misconception is that a farming potion is poured onto your crops, rather than into your mouth. While it might sound sensible - it's the crops that are growing, not you - it fundamentally misunderstands what the farming potion does.

The farming potion increases the experience you receive when you farm. It achieves this by making you sensitive to the wants and needs of your plants. You become intensely aware of them. You will know when even a single aphid lands on a leaf; when the last drop has been siphoned from the soil; when a potato wants to hear you sing. You are attuned to your crops, to the point that you might even find kinship with them. If you begin sleeping in your cabbage patch, you should consider lowering your consumption.
}}

The Children of Shadows used to try brew large quantities of this potion every time they went off on a mission, so that they would have the edge were they ever caught. Many a guard could attest to the power of this potion, but fortunately it didn’t make up for a general lack of melee skill.

{{Crafting Tree|Lesser Magic Potion}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
Although humans cannot use magic without runes, they can become quite proficient conduits for power. A wizard and a farmer, when possessing the same runes, do not produce the same results, the former far outshines the former. 

This made some farmers pretty upset. For years they had ranted to their cows and sheep about how wizards were just snooty uppity types with shiny rocks. Yet, faced with this revelation, there was no denying that a farmer and a wizard simply weren’t equals in disguise. 

One farmer wanted to level the playing field and brought in a local witch who was had a grudge against the snooty men in blue robes. 

Between the two of them, they found a way to improve a person’s connection to the magic within them via a magical potion. Those who drank it cast spells more efficiently and with greater skill than they ever could before. 

The farmer wanted to use this new advantage to put the wizards in their place, raze down the tower and claim magic a tool of the people. Unfortunately, the witch saw a different future, one that sparkled with glittering gold coins. 

She died happily, wealthier than she had ever dreamed, surrounded by adoring young suiters who wanted a piece of her inheritance. The farmer died after being trampled to death by cows that were tired of his grumbling. 
}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
It is almost imperceptible, but mystic cloth hums. It's the magical resonance: the elemental threads pushing against each other as their charge shifts. That oscillation also means that there is a lightly massaging effect on the wearer. It's entirely possible to feel calm from the vibrations as you stride into battle.

You might also be mistaken for thinking that mystic cloth is blue. On a microscopic level, it's actually a multitude of colours, combining to form the illusion of blue. As a magician once told me, it's the same effect as a blue sky: it is the result of all the colours in the world combining to make wondrous azure.

|mat1qty = 2

|mat3 = Clean Water
|mat3qty = 1
|output1 = Plant Cure
}}

===Recipe tree===
{{Crafting Tree|Plant Cure}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
Fashioned from clean water, weeds and animal bones, this mixture leeches out the vitality from those ingredients and transfers it to the sick and dying plants in your care. Cooked over a range, this concoction was first thought to be the domain of druids and herblore masters, but in truth it was a cook that put the pieces together. 

Old mother Potterington was much beloved by the people of Bramblemead. On weekends, when people allowed themselves brief breaks form their toils, she would whip up a great batch of something delicious and simmering, and neighbouring farmers would drop by for a meal. 

This kindness extended not only to people, but to her garden and farming patches too. She whipped up a broth so infused with nutrients, that Brassica Prime himself is said to have blessed it. When fed to plants, their withering and wilting leaves would stiffen and return to vibrancy, life and vitality theirs once again.

Now you can brew such a concoction yourself, so that your plants might always live their healthiest days.
}}

{{Journal entry|
As with many physical activities, you can over-exert yourself when mining. Lactic acid builds up in the muscles, sweat clouds the vision, and an accidental pickaxe swing can lodge in the head. A mining potion addresses all of these shortcomings. Lactic acid and sweat forms slowly. The likelihood of accidents is reduced.

What it can't do is improve the quality or amount of ore. Pour it in your mouth or pour it on the deposit: it won't matter. No mining potion is going to help you there.

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
Cathan’s challenge horn design is a collection of materials hastily thrown together. A dragon’s tooth, carved with dragonkin sigils as well as metal wires used to connect them together –  like a spiderweb lattice, glistening with traces of magical power.

When placed in the dragonkin altar, the horn acts as a focus point for the magical power stored within the tower, sending an invisible beacon off into the air, in a perfect draconic pitch.

Velgar has been summoned many times before. By heroes, kings, warriors and gods, and yet still the tower stands.

Be ready, when you send out the call.
}}

The crystal tree is a magical thing, a native to the elven world Tarddiad and brought to Gielinor when the elves migrated. Unlike most seeds it is nourished not by soil, nor sunlight, but by music. Elf song reaches into the crystal, creating a harmonious resonance that causes the crystal to thrive.

As well as growing trees, this seed can also be sung into specific shapes and forms, becoming a tool or weapon of great power.

===== User:RSDWArchive/Resource/Bloodwood Sap =====
{{Infobox Item
|name = Bloodwood Sap
|image = Bloodwood Sap.png
|type = Resource
|description = Harvested from bloodwood trees, found in the toxic swamp in Ghornfell.
|weight = 2.0
|stacklimit = 99
}}
'''Bloodwood Sap''' is a resource item.

==Products==
{{Uses material list|Bloodwood Sap}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
Bloodwood trees are a genuinely horrible creation. Their very existence a wound in the decency of the world, because this tree grows only in places steeped in violence and death.

The biggest bloodwood trees tower over battlefields. Sinewy spiderlike branches cast shade over the homes of serial killers, and you should never trust anyone that can grow one in their garden.

Leech-like roots soak up the suffering, sorrow and cruelty that has seeped into the soil, and then converts that misery into a sticky red sap of raw emotion. This sap can be used to amplify feelings, to convey anger, fear or hatred, across a much greater range.

The dragonkin Lacrussa was very fond of this medium, and used it’s power to shackle dragons to her will.

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
There is a curious trend on Gielinor, whereby the most fragile fighters - archers and magic users - are the easiest to spot. From blue dragonhide to mystic robes, the fashion is to wear garish colours as if the rules of the animal kingdom apply. But no, archers and magic users aren't poisonous, venomous or hoping to be mistaken for a bee.

We wonder why that lack of subtlety might be. In the case of blue dragons and their scales, perhaps it's a cruel joke played by the dragonkin. They have seen that humans keep killing their creations, wearing their hides as trophies. They've got their revenge by way of a generous use of the rainbow.

{{Journal entry|
Blue dragon dust is one of those things where you wonder who invented it, and what curious sequence of events led to it happening. Some unknown person had the wherewithal to strip a dragon of dragon scales, crush those scales in a pestle and mortar, then apply the resulting dust to a potion. Not only that, they downed said potion and stood in the path of a dragon. Does that not seem inexorably mad to you? 

But thank you, inexorably mad person, because now we have this potent ingredient which can protect a person from dragonfire. You have been forgotten in time, but your blue dusty legacy lives on.

{{Journal entry|
Not all cats are terrified of crossbows, though most of the Bramblemead population quickly learned to fear them. Some cats could see their merit but were painfully aware of their human pet’s limited imagination.

Mittens was the lifelong owner of Gothren Actillian. A blacksmith’s cat, he had learned how to keep the forge fires perfectly hot by playfully jumping on the bellows periodically – something his pet seemed to enjoy. He knew the right length of time a sword should be cooled for and would make sure his human stuck to that timing by offering useful alarms made of glorious clattering things.

But blurite? That was a new one. Mittens could see there was little value to the metal, beyond some weird human aesthetic that he did not understand, yet there was some potential to the construction. With carefully timed meows, and some creative knocking over of reagents, Mittens was able to engineer a crossbow of superior design, worthy of his cherished pet.

{{Journal entry|
Following certain incidents with cats and crossbow limbs, a superstition began to build in Bramblemead about the danger of crossbows and felines. It was considered bad luck to house a cat in the same home as a crossbow, with reasoning ranging from the safety of the cat, to the safety of the human population should the cats rise up and develop opposable thumbs.

Whilst harmless at first, when the need for crossbows grew due to the conflict with the garou, cats found themselves with fewer and fewer homes willing to house them. Over the years this led to domestic cats being a rare sight in Bramblemead.

It also created a deep-seated resentment in the cats, and they plotted their revenge. Most would tell you that cats had nothing to do with the destruction of Bramblemead and the Brynmoor settlements, yet if you ask a cat, they will simply purr with a sinister grin on their face.

In the Highlands of Ghornfell lay the bones of titan wyrms. These dread creatures were once the pride of the dragonkin forces. Massive beasts, with wingspans that blotted out the sun and claws that could tear down a fortress. They were destroyed in a cataclysmic battle against a powerful mage with a command over lightning, who summoned a terrible storm that still rages to this day.

The wyrms are dead now. At least, we hope they are. All that remain are their bones. The teeth are particularly prized and are a vital component in some dragonkin craftwork.
}}

{{Journal entry|
Do not pity the dragonwolf. Oh, you don’t? That’s fine then. Yes, horrible little blighters aren’t they? Their teeth are too jagged and they’re far too aggressive for my tastes. Still, apparently deadly critters don’t just want to roll over and die so you can harvest their skin, who’d have thought?

The dragonwolf is an experiment that didn’t quite go right. It wasn’t wrong, exactly, it was certainly a step in the direction their creator wanted, but like most Dragonkin experiments, they was never “good enough”. Too warm-blooded. Too fluffy. Too weak.

Fortunately, the crafters in Emberwood were not quite so picky. They found that hide to be incredibly durable and hardy, whilst remaining surprisingly flexible. They would craft wonderous outfits from the tanned leather, trying to emulate their winged overseers.
}}

==Item sources==
{{Drop sources list|Ectoplasm}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
There are many theories on what ectoplasm is, each as disturbing as the last. Some say that it’s emotion, condensed over years of existence. Others think that it’s some sort of infection of the soul, as only the undead seem to produce it.

In truth, ectoplasm is none of these. It’s the outer shell of a soul, the skin more or less, and acts as a sort of lubrication between the flesh and the spirit. Tiny bits of reality combine with the immaterial otherness of the underworld and congeal into a sort of spiritual mixture that ghosts and other undead find incredible useful.

Necromancers prize the stuff, finding a myriad of uses for it. Most people find it weird and decidedly “icky”.
}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
Used to craft Fire arrows.

Some people just like to watch the world burn… and you can too, with these new handy fire oils! That’s right, just lob one of these beauties at your enemies and watch them ignite. Enjoy their screams as their skin boils away and breathe in the delightful aroma of a fresh barbecue!

Fire oil, like snake oil, was once the creation of a travelling merchant to Ashenfall. She had journeyed to Brynmoor alongside some of the Saradominist settlers, and with her she brought pungent unguents, elucidating elixirs, marvellous medicines, and weapons of localised destruction.

When her wares summoned the call for refunds, she would dazzle the onlookers with a sudden fiery display and then disappear into the alleyways until she had been forgotten. She would then return in one of a staggering array of disguises, until the tragic day when her wagon hit a pothole during a quick getaway and her many, many, bottles of fire oils decided to sing the song of their people.

Fortunately, even though she and everything she owned, tragically found itself reduced to smouldering atoms, her recipe lived on and found more conventional uses.
}}

{{Drop sources list|Green Dragon Hide}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
Dragons are never fond of surrendering their natural armour, a natural feature they’ve used to great advantage.

In the earliest days of the Dragonkin experiments, the scales of a dragon were something to be proud of. They would turn away blade and arrow with equal skill, and even magic struggled to pierce their natural defences.

Still, this wasn’t good enough for their makers. Lacrussa, herself, saw the hide of dragons as a promising start, but little more, and she would strive to forge newer and more resilient scales on her creations. The green dragons were, in her opinion, some of the weakest of the dragons, and she only kept them around because her sibling enjoyed the glittering green reflections of the sunlight on their scales.
}}

Is it ingenuity of hubris to refine the mighty scales of a dragon down into this thick and sturdy leather?

To the Wild Knights it was the natural order. Hides became leather, which became a resilient second skin they would wear whilst riding into battle. Favoured by archers and scouts due to the nimble flexibility of the scales, whilst still acting as a resilient bulwark against sword, arrow and claw alike.

To the people of Emberwood village, however, such sights were akin to blasphemy. Whilst the green dragons showed little mercy, the villagers loved and adored their majestic draconic protectors, Imaru and Xikotal, and they thought that wearing the skin of their kind might potentially cause offence.

|stacklimit = 99
}}
'''Hollow Bark''' is a resource item.

==Products==
{{Uses material list|Hollow Bark}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
It is perhaps strange that bark could be referred to as hollow. It’s generally extracted in strips, or patches, but nothing that could act as a container. Indeed there would need to be an entire tree without a centre to make it hollow, and that’s exactly the case here.

When the withering began it was souls that suffered first, torn away and dragged into the underworld to be consumed by the cursed dragon. Yet, as time drew on, Imaru’s hunger did not diminish, only grow, and so the world itself began to suffer.

Things taste worse in Fellhollow. Dreams are vapid and empty, if you have them at all. A campire feels colder, even if it warms you just as well as before. Because the substance, the soul of that thing if you will, is being consumed.

Hollow bark comes from a tree that has been hollowed out from within. Its insides less than they should be, weaker and wrong. As awful as this is, it makes the bark develop in strange ways desirable by skilled mages with a poor sense of fashion.
}}

It is unsurprising that irit grows in Fellhollow, considering it has such a close association with the dead. Whereas normal irit grows around graveyards and near the temples of death deities, the irit in Fellhollow grows everywhere.

Yet, unlike its leafier version, the irit here is twisted and sharp. It is formed of thorny roots that writhe out of the ground and must be cut down to access the herb beneath. After all, the dead in Fellhollow refuse to stay buried without a fight, why wouldn’t the irit react the same?
}}

===Recipe tree===
{{Crafting Tree|Iron Crossbow Limbs}}

==Products==
{{Uses material list|Iron Crossbow Limbs}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
Following certain incidents with cats and crossbow limbs, a superstition began to build in Bramblemead about the danger of crossbows and felines. It was considered bad luck to house a cat in the same home as a crossbow, with reasoning ranging from the safety of the cat, to the safety of the human population should the cats rise up and develop opposable thumbs.

Whilst harmless at first, when the need for crossbows grew due to the conflict with the garou, cats found themselves with fewer and fewer homes willing to house them. Over the years this led to domestic cats being a rare sight in Bramblemead.

It also created a deep-seated resentment in the cats, and they plotted their revenge. Most would tell you that cats had nothing to do with the destruction of Bramblemead and the Brynmoor settlements, yet if you ask a cat, they will simply purr with a sinister grin on their face.
}}

{{Crafting Tree|Mithril Bar}}

==Products==
{{Uses material list|Mithril Bar}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
In the Third Age on Ashenfall, mithril was incredibly desirable. It was only available in small quantities then, as its scarcity - perhaps inevitably - made it the fashion of the time. High-priests would incorporate it into their rosaries. Community leaders would wear it as brooches. It was rare enough that people would comment when they saw it. "Ooh, Rosie's doing well for herself". That sort of thing. 

The idea of a mithril bar would have been mind-boggling to anyone in the Third Age. No matter their alignment, they'd have stabbed you in the belly and run away cackling with it. But here you are with an entire ingot. Take a moment and consider yourself a Third Age king. 
}}

{{Uses material list|Mystic Thread}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
There are many steps to making mystic robes - fibres to thread, thread to cloth, cloth to robes - but you would be wise not to skip any of them. Habberdash the Impatient, a magician who lived in Temple Woods, attempted to make his robes solely from thread. He would wrap himself, round and round, with spool after spool of mystic thread, and then attempt battle.

You can imagine how it went. He got snagged on a goblin's helmet and quickly unwound, mid-battle. We're not sure who would have been more shocked: Habberdash, who promptly got stabbed in the gut, or the goblin, who was confronted with a wizard in his undergarments.
}}

The priests of Emberwood created this oil to assist in funerary rites, the strange scent of the oil would help the dead pass on when cremated and, crucially, in the time of the Withering, the bodies would be reduced to ash, unable to get up and cause further trouble.

Originally this oil used pressed olives, and the influence of the gods to create an oil that would burn a body sufficiently to avoid the dead rising. As the Withering increased and civilisation began to fall into ruin, the priests found alternative methods to create a sufficiently strong flame.

{{Journal entry|
The heart is a pump, nothing more, designed to push precious blood around the circulatory system, so that our weak and feeble frames can function. Yet, metaphysically, it is the most important organ, for it houses our emotional centre, the very essence of what makes us human.

A withered heart isn’t just a heart that has languished. Nor is it just a heart that is drained of blood. No, a withered heart has had all the humanity leeched from it, emptied of emotion, or connection, of self.

This process is imperfect, of course, and tiny fragments of soul-matter remains, that can be refined and extracted from the heart. Withdrawing the last remnants of what made the owner “them”.

{{Journal entry|
In Fellhollow the dead refuse to stay buried. All save one.

Jenniva Milgrim was a fan of her rest, she liked nothing more than to ensconce herself within her blankets and disappear into a nice dream. Mornings became lost to her and soon evenings joined her campaign and she would spend most of her existence in the myriad worlds of her subconscious.

Then, one cruel day, she died. A victim of one of the first waves of the risen dead. She died, then awoke again as one of the rampaging horde.

Except she did not rampage like the others. She did not cross the lands in search of souls to claim, or flesh to consume. Instead she sought comfort once again in blankets and cushions, but found that sleep was denied her, as dreams are the province of the living.

There was precious little capability for thought in what remained of her brain, but a singular idea took hold. Since one buried the dead, perhaps that was where the dead could dream? Six feet under the soil, in blissful sleep.

So it was, that Jenniva became the first of the dead to bury themselves, using this very tool to do so.

It is said, that if you can find her grave, buried deep in the woods, you can still hear her snoring.

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
It's not entirely clear why a staff helps channel magic. Druids would claim that it was because they were working with nature, aligning the magic spell through the plant's systems. Members of the wizard's guild argued that it wasn't that the wood itself was special but that they worked as a focus, helping to channel the mind of the wizard rather than the wood being special.

The inclusion of rune essence in a staff's design is a testament to the meticulous craftsmanship and artistry involved. This essence, often crushed into a fine powder and dispersed throughout the wood's careful grooves, creates a magical circulatory system within the staff. In this way, the staff becomes a living entity, with the wizard as its beating heart, channelling power through its veins to unleash upon its foes. 

A staff is rarely helpful for less violent magic. They are brute force weapons, where magic is forced into elemental blasts, obliterating the target. More subtle spells rely on the caster's will and are powered directly by their magical skill. 
}}

{{Journal entry|
An ash shortbow is the first weapon most young archers train with. It’s easy to make and, therefore, not so problematic if it breaks during training. Human villagers would often craft their first bows together under the tutelage of a visiting Wild Knight. They would use branches that had naturally fallen from the trees and carefully whittle them into the bow’s limbs. Bowstrings would be created by gathering flax from the nearby fields and spinning them into thin but hardy threads. 

Most would break on first use. Some would break before the first arrow was fired. Still, village youngsters would laugh at their misfortunes and start the whole process again. Each time improving. Each new bow sturdier than the last.

The stranger the wood, the more powerful the magic. It’s unsure why this is, but it’s been true since magic was first discovered. When used as a tool for destructive magic, Garou druids learned the power of blightwood. 

Ashien, a legendary druid among the garou, was among the first to wield such a weapon. As the story goes, they were wandering the swamps when the goddess Lougrim came to her in a vision and gave her a quest. Ashien was to journey deep into the swamps and do battle with a demon that dwelled within. 

They found the demon; it emerged out of the fog with a chilling screech and destroyed their staff with a single swing of its blade-like claw. In panic, Ashien blindly reached for the nearest weapon, the root of a swamp tree that had fallen in the mud. Through it, they channeled their will to survive, and it burst free of the branch as a flash of lightning. 

The creature burned beneath Ashien’s gaze, vanishing back into the mists as if it never were. 

Since then, garou druids would favour blightwood when crafting a staff.

===Recipe tree===
{{Crafting Tree|Blurite Crossbow}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
For centuries alchemists have yearned to create gold. To transmute base metals into something pure and shiny. While gold is the goal, there are other, stranger metals, along the way, and what could be more bizarre than a bar of purest blue.

Blurite is defined by its colour. It’s in the very name. Yet it offers no real magical, or alchemical value beyond other metals. Artistic, perhaps, it was favoured by poets, bards and artisans of more eccentric tastes, but it still offered little in the way of superior weaponry.

That was until Gothren Actillian took a crack at it. He was an blacksmith, obsessed with the less desired metals and materials. He would hunt for hours in the darkest caverns for slivers of blue, ignoring glittering silver and gold. To him the metal was special, radiant and beautiful. The hues generated a joy in him that he could not describe, and he longed to craft it into something befitting its splendour. He was delighted when he found the ore glittering away in a hidden dragonkin vault in Ghornfell's central region. 

He was never any good with a sword, and his magical prowess wouldn’t frighten a kebbit. Yet crossbows, those he could wield. He was a skilled marksman, and could knock an apple from a chinchompa’s head before it exploded.

The crossbow, blue as the ocean, caused much mockery from his companions, yet their mockery soon died as he speared a bolt through the heart of a dragon. Something all of their weapons had failed to do.

He was just disappointed that the dragon’s scales were green and went searching for that ever elusive blue.
}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
Animal bones are surprisingly durable, especially those found on Ashenfall. The magic of the continent seeps into their marrow, slowly strengthening them and making them tougher. This goes some way to explaining the ferocity of ordinarily docile creatures, but it also helps when crafting tools. 

Cows and similar beasts were celebrated in the age of Guthix. The people of Brynmoor preferred to take an animal’s life only on the hunt or after long years of service. When an animal passed, it was thanked for its sacrifice, and the materials helped strengthen the village. 

A club forged of bone was a simple tool but one that made defending the village much easier. Roving beasts were easily pushed back, and the village was protected by the animal’s last gifts. 
}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
Before he learned to use the bow, Ulv survived with simple daggers of bone. He lived outside the village, cast out for his silence and strange ways. Ulv did not follow the polite nonsense of human society, nor did he seem to care for their troubles. The boy was happy just to survive and whittle small carvings of animals from fallen branches. 

He hunted silently, using the daggers to slay small prey such as rabbits and chickens. He ate what he needed and sold the excess at the markets for enough coin to purchase simple clothes and tools. 

When he was thirteen, he was beaten by bandits and left for dead. But a Wild Knight found him and brought him to safety. Recovering in the knight’s home, Ulv would be taught how to use a bow, a skill he soon mastered. 

When a wolf attacked Bramblemead, this outcast slew it. Villagers thanked him for his bravery and asked him what he wanted as a reward. He refuted their offers and asked only for the wolf’s skull in return. He fashioned it into a mask that he chose as a new face, one he wore away from the village that had spurned him. 
}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
The members of the Wild Knights who trained with melee weapons, generally found themselves the victors in friendly sparring matches against their companions. The reasoning was simple – shields. A shield could turn aside blade, arrow and spell, with equal skill and it left their enemy vulnerable to counterattack. This sense of superiority began to change from friendly competition, into a sense of smugness capable of souring many friendships.

Roliker Hallister was particularly obnoxious. His skill with sword and shield was admittedly impressive. At the age of twenty he could best even some of the commanders of the Wild Knights in single combat. Healthy pride twisted into smug egoism, which then rotted down into unpleasant superiority. He was rude. He was dismissive. He was pretty much an obnoxious nightmare to be around.

Which is why he was very surprised by the bolt in his shoulder, and why no one else seemed too inclined to help him out. Vanida Mox was a skilled archer and inventor. She was quick to learn, quick to study and she had the enviable ability to see when something was wrong and work to find a solution. Popular with the other knights, because she would work with them, share accolades, and stand for what the order truly meant – a barrier between the world and the wild.

As Roliker’s ego grew and grew, she realised that the archers in the order were at a significant disadvantage in close combat. At range, they were obviously superior, but as all the sparring matches were held in the courtyard, there was precious little distance available. So she began working on a device that would deliver the power of an arrow but allowing one hand free to hold a shield.

It was very effective.

She named it a “cross-bow”, because she was very very angry when she unloaded it into the cloud of smugness known as Roliker. Later that name would be attributes to the mechanical structure of the device, but now you know better.
}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
Bronze is a common enough alloy, a combination of copper and tin. Durable, defiant, and deadly in the right hands. For Mia Larsdottir, it was a bronze dagger that pierced her heart, cutting her life short at the age of twenty-one. 

As the first of the Amalgamated, she had never expected to reach any of the milestones her peers traditionally followed. She did not expect to be married, and she never let herself dream of being a mother. She thought, perhaps, that she might be allowed to carve a quiet little place for herself, somewhere with room for cats. 

But a bronze dagger stole that dream from her. 

Her killer was never brought to justice, though there were rumours about who they were. Her father, being the chief suspect, ashamed as he was to bring the first of the unnatural Amalgamated into the world. He denied it, of course, but he never held a funeral for her. Instead, her body was left in the forest, where nature might put her at peace. 
}}

{{Journal entry|
The Wild Knight Kessel was unusual in her choice of weaponry. Where most of the order chose to wield bows, daggers, or swift blades, Kessel favoured a bronze greatsword. On the battlefield, she hefted it across her shoulders, never letting the hilt leave her grip.  

As one of the Amalgamated, Kessel’s skin glowed like burning coals, her battle scars resembling faint reddish embers. She harnessed this heat, channelling it through her sword. Her magic set the blade ablaze, a sight that struck terror into the hearts of her enemies. With great arcs of red flame, she cleaved through enemy forces, incinerating them as she severed their limbs from their bodies. 

On one fateful day, she would use this technique against a force of garou hunters. The battle was long, hard, and brutal, and both sides faced great casualties. But it was when she sliced her blade across the young garou prince that war was inevitable.
}}

Where bone and stone fail, metal provides. The bronze axe is strong enough to withstand greater force than its predecessors and can break through the bark of some of the strongest trees. On Ashenfall, nature has been hardened by the ambient magic, the bark of trees makes them resistant to most attacks. Yet, the bronze axe breaks through that barrier, not by magic, nor by cunning, but by sheer durability and resolve.

The lumberjacks of Brynmoor favoured bronze axes over iron. While iron was stronger and felled a tree quicker, the relatively cheapness and availability of copper and tin ore, made it a much more cost effective choice.

The villagers disapproved when the leadership pushed for iron in everything. They felt that bronze was more than enough for the village needs. But the lord wanted progress, and didn’t care about the price

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
Legend has it that when the first sword was forged, Guthix wept. Given that Guthix commissioned warriors and soldiers and, at times, encouraged war, this is perhaps not a truthful statement. Yet, the sword is a weapon with a singular purpose: to end the life of another. Of course, this is true of all weapons, but none so iconic as the blade. 

Children would play in the street, striking one another with wooden blades rather than clubs or daggers. They would pretend to be knights rather than brigands or priests. To wield a blade was a sign of bravery. To draw a sword was the hero’s stance. 

War shatters all childhood dreams. 

Nothing removes the nonsense of chivalry more than seeing the life leaving the eyes of a terrified foe. A sword puts the wielder in that moment, forcing them to face what it is they destroy. To understand that there are no such things as heroes, only warrior against warrior and knowing that one of them will fall. 
}}

{{Journal entry|
Doric would be the first person to praise the simple hammer. It is a large solid chunk of metal attached to a long haft, allowing the weapon to benefit from the unmistakable might of physics. Weight and speed are a terrifying combination. 

Dwarves, in particular, favour this weapon. They feel it speaks to their long-held desire to shape metal by pounding into shape by sheer strength alone. They apply the same logic to their enemies, beating them into a shape that the dwarves feel suits their enemies better.  

There were once dwarves on Ashenfall who were masters of this technique. However, when the humans began their infighting, and Guthix turned away from them, they vanished deeper into the continent, leaving behind a shroud of mystery in search of something extraordinary. 

They found it and have never returned.

Mouldfinger never wanted to be chief, unlike the other goblins she aspired to be just a background character – happy and forgotten while she worked on her own things. She enjoyed working with wood, bone and, on those special occasions, metal.

She crafted a sword, a simple blade that was sturdy and strong, and the other goblins went wild because of it. Seeing its sharpness, they became convinced it was magical, or imbued with the power of their draconic overlord. It wasn’t, it was just very well made.

She was made chieftain after the others challenged her, and her sharpened blade cut easily through their defenses. A fate she had never wanted, and a fate she could never escape.

|output1 = Crystal Bow
}}

===Recipe tree===
{{Crafting Tree|Crystal Bow}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
Crystal bows are not crafted but sung into existence. Harmonies are layered over one another to teach the weapon a story so that it might understand why it needs to be strong. Traditionally, the plight of the elves, their loneliness without their goddess, and the many dangers they must face are sung. 

The shimmering substance they’re made from is traditionally a shard of the elven goddess Seren, left behind when her crystal form shattered at the end of the Third Age God Wars. 

This bow isn’t the same material, and the song is different, too. There’s no divine essence in the crystal, no lament of the elves. Instead, it is sung memories of a lifetime together, distilled down into facets reflecting in the crystalline flaws. In the moonlight, those facets sparkle like tiny stars held within glass—moments of hardship, conflict, happiness, and grief. 

It is music as a weapon, with memory as the handle and sorrow as the string. 
}}

Normal weapons had no effect on the creature, yet for some reason the bone bolts fired by this crossbow were enough to unravel its material form, banishing it back to the darkness.

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
Rasthin was a powerful sorceress, even among the dragonkin. She had mastered all manner of spells, and was even schooled in the techniques from the previous Revision.

Still, magic as an art was largely looked down upon by dragonkin society. It was considered vulgar, and the obsession of children, and alchemy and science was the real way forward. In part it’s because of the connection between magic and the hated Elder Gods, and the dragonkin feared rousing, further, their anger.

But Rasthin knew the value of magic, as did the other members of her group. She created a staff, forged from glittering crystal and anima-infused iron, which allowed her to channel her magic into powerful spells.

Yet, even with a weapon as powerful as this, she discarded her magic when she uncovered the power of Ashenfall – preferring, instead, to enjoy her newfound connection with elemental flame.

Still, the remnants of the staff bristle with potential, and while they may never reach the might of their ancestor, they remain powerful magic tools just waiting to be crafted.
}}

{{Journal entry|
Viika was never fond of creating dragons, they thought the process was cruel and unbecoming. When an egg was laid, Viika saw in that moment both the egg and the dragon it would become. They saw past and presence at the same time, and they grieved the creature before it had even hatched.

They pleaded with their sibling, and with the other Dragonkin, to change their treatment of the beasts. But Viika’s curse, like so many Seers, was to be ignored by their kindred.

A rare egg hatched once, containing a dragon with white scales like pearls. The dragon was infused with magic and possessing a power capable of travelling to other worlds, where she might have lived a happier life. But Viika wept, for they knew she would manage no such ending.

Viika kept the hatchling company. Treated them like their dearest friend, and held them softly when Lacrussa’s need for knowledge, took the dragon’s last breath.

The Seer kept only a single keepsake – a blade carved from the tooth of their white-scaled friend. A dagger capable of terrible damage, but as fragile as the friendship that it reminded them of.

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
Contrary to popular belief, a goblin is as smart as any other species. It was Bandos that instilled within them the notion that intelligence was a sin, and demonstrating your education was something to be discouraged. As a result, goblins often go out of their way to make themselves seem less intelligent than they really are.

Hence “swingslash”, the name given to this axe because of how it swings through the air, slashing anything it hits. It’s so reductive and silly, it can only be an overcorrection, a desperate attempt by the creator to seem dumber than they are.

You can ignore, therefore the curve of the blade and the sharpness of the edge, created by carefully thought-out techniques that make the weapon deadlier than those before them. The name, chosen by the blacksmith, so none might accuse them of the crime of being smart.
}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
While metal may be the preferred choice of weapon makers, the granite maul stands as a testament to the raw power of stone. This legendary weapon, revered among hammer wielders, is nothing more than a massive, heavy stone affixed to a stick. Yet, in the hands of a skilled wielder, it becomes a force of unparalleled destruction. 

It was developed by ancient dwarves long ago after one dwarf got fed up with the rock hammer he was using to fight a nest of gargoyles. The beasts were strong and numerous, and their skin was almost impenetrable to conventional weaponry; only rock hammers seemed to hurt them. In frustration, one dwarf took the biggest hunk of granite he could find and turned it into a legend. 

Since that moment, the weapon has been refined, using various special components to make it more wieldy in combat. The original creator having done himself an injury with the recoil. 
}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
Lougrim was a moon deity, born to a cold world of soft silvers and silence. Her people lived lives of quiet contemplation, each moment spent wondering about the next. They were passive, soft spoken and sedentary, which drove Lougrim wild.

When a doorway to another world appeared and a grieving god wandered through it, Lougrim took the opportunity to run. To flee to another place, and live a life that she could endure.

History skips the next bit. Her closest allies have never learned what elevated her from her previous form to that of the goddess of the hunt, but whatever it is was profound enough to change her completely. She no longer resembled her silent kindred. She was quiet, yes, but in the way a tiger is moments before the kill. She is contemplative, true, but it was the stillness of a spider waiting for its prey.

When she found the garou, she knew she had found her real kindred. They were violent and deadly, and they yearned for the hunt. When she took her place as their goddess, she focused and refined them, creating hunters that were capable of felling almost any prey.

Yet still she kept the moon as her symbol, a reminder of her home and how far she has come since leaving it.

Now her priests bear the symbol, atop their staves and as the focus on their altars. They accept and revere Kuldra as their High Queen, yet they grieve the moon goddess that made them who they are today.
}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
Gahl was a garou druid who lost everyone he knew. In the wars inflicted on his people by the other races of Ashenfall, he grew jaded with the cruelty he saw all around him. This reached its peak when he found a garou village in ruins and goblins dancing and laughing as they threatened a newly born pup, in her crib.

The village is gone now, dragged beneath the soil. Gahl’s vengeance unleashed upon the goblins, erasing them from existence. He took the child as his own and raised her in a way alien to his people – he raised her with love.

She had no talent for magic, and could not learn his druid spells, so he taught her how to hunt with a bow, and she was a natural. Dahnu, as he named her, made a bow out of the first deer she and her father had hunted and that bow became a symbol to all she encountered.

In time she would claim a king’s seat. Defeating the prior monarch with reason and wit. Charming him out of his power and offering her people another way.  

Her people thrived, making her father proud.

Until Velgar brought her reign to an end.
}}

{{Journal entry|
The essence of an undead dragon, distilled down into a blade. What could go wrong?

This weapon is cold to the touch in ways far beyond chilling. Holding it feels as if you’re out in the cold, with no shelter to protect you. Exposure in the palm of your hand.

Worse than the cold, is the hunger. This scimitar wants to cut, to stab, to slice and to maim. It wants to see your enemies bleed so that it can feast on their suffering. Imaru may be dead, but her hunger is eternal and you feel it infecting you with each swing of the blade.

Still, the power of this blade makes it almost worth it. What’s a little hunger when faced with the destruction of your foes? Lament later, surely, and revel now in the carnage. Perhaps there’s a little dragon in you too?

{{Journal entry|
Iron turned the war against the garou more than some people would like to admit. They would claim superior training, tactics, and skills of their soldiers, but the truth is far simpler. Iron was strong and iron weapons were brutal.

Ranged weapons proved effective against the garou leadership, bound as they were by strict codes of honour. A thane was a deadly opponent up close, but if you could pierce their internal organs before they were within a swing’s reach, then they were no more dangerous than any other beast. It is perhaps no surprise then, that there was a race to create weapons to challenge them.

The people of Brynmoor had learned of a Wild Knight invention, a weapon that would allow one to deliver powerful ranged attacks, whilst still allowing the bearer to wield a shield. They took this design, studied and refined it and then upgraded it to include the power of iron weapons.

Garou numbers dropped rapidly as a result, turning the war heavily against them. In their desperation, the garou turned to their goddess and she, in turn, sought allies with deadlier weapons still.
}}

{{Journal entry|
Few sights are as intimidating as a great axe hefted toward you. It can only be carried in a pose that exudes raw strength, and a bearer of such a weapon can rarely look meek. 

Bandos was also a fan of the aesthetic. While he favoured the sheer brutality of the kyzaj, he chose to wield a great axe against Velgar. He stormed Brakka’s Folly, great axe in hand, and challenged the dragon to single combat. A god versus a dragon, the outcome felt obvious, yet it did not play out how Bandos expected. 

It should have been easy. Yet Velgar’s stone-touched flesh turned away blows, and his poisonous breath leeched even Bandos’ strength. Bandos cut a great scar down Velgar’s side, yet the wound was not fatal, and the counterattack sent Bandos reeling. 

He never surrendered, but there was no victory for the big high war god. He sounded a tactical retreat, seeking superior tactics – far, far away. 
}}

Necromancy was rare on Ashenfall, though not unheard of. Two necromancers had been reported to the order, one a girl with a knack for bones and another who whispered with the dead. He joined the Wild Knight commander, Vemmeck, in their siege against a northern garou stronghold. With countless goblins at their side, their victory was almost assured. Yet a single druid’s magic held the forces at bay until Sir Lear learned how ineffective his mace was against the scales of a dragon.

Alric relished walking among the maple trees. For so much of his life, he had been encased in stone and surrounded by essence: working long hours in the keep. But the maples were for thinking. 

In his twilight years, Alric carried a maple staff with him: the Subjugation Staff. It was a crutch for an old man, yes, but it was also a way to bring the grove with him. When he couldn't muster the energy to visit his favoured trees, he carried a remnant with him.  
}}

{{Journal entry|
A supple wood, is the maple. When cut into long, reed-like lengths, it can be formed into a worthy longbow. The process also releases syrup - a treat for a day's fletching. Not enough to make a maple toastie, mind, but enough to leave a sweet taste in the mouth.

Bramblemead was often the venue for archery competitions, and the maple longbows would be out in force. Etched into the trophy, you would find many Rasmodels. They were a noble bloodline on Ashenfall, and would often add to their reputation by earning combat trophies.

{{Journal entry|
Putrilius, the cthonian demon, will tell you that any living thing can be possessed. If needs must, a cthonian can be a cockroach or spider, for a time. 

In one desperate moment, after the Dreaming Stone was shattered, Putrilius was forced to possess a maple tree. It wasn't an experience she enjoyed. Most curiously, she found themselves aligning to the maple's inner cadence. Everything slowed. Putrilius barely registered a thought in two years.

What woke Putrilius was a logging axe. Their maple body was toppled and then fletched into an armature. For a moment, as Putrilius's life faded from the wood, she was a shortbow. 

It was the closest she had come to dying. With a cognitive spark, she moved from the bow to a passing hound before all her lifeforce ebbed away.
}}

{{Journal entry|
A mithril crossbow is the standard issue for any modern Black Knight. If you showed capability, then you might be promoted to Black Knight Sniper, and that came with the Black Sniper Crossbow. But for the average Black Knight, the crossbow was a long-kept friend. 

The crossbow's main purpose was to stop demons in their tracks. The Zamorakian magi claimed to keep their demon hordes under control, but demons tested that claim.

The crossbow had other uses. Remove the bolt, rest the crossbow on the floor stock-upwards, and you had a stool. Sit on the floor and it was a headrest. 

You could also waste time shooting ravens. Shooting the red, glowing ravens was an immediate dismissal, however. Alric demanded they were protected, for reasons that he never expanded on.
}}

Lord Rasmodel wasn't one for naming his weapons. He found the custom a little juvenile. But when his thoughts were elsewhere, you might see him pat the head of the warhammer. There was kinship there, even if he wouldn't admit it.

Necromancy isn’t inherently evil, despite what some of the scriptures might say. Whilst some cruelly force the dead into service, others make bargains and pacts with spirits, offering them a chance to influence the mortal world again, rather than simply watch events unfold.

In Fellhollow a small group of mages encountered a smoking fissure in the earth. From it they heard strange whispering voices in the darkness, promising them power and knowledge. Greedily they listened, making pacts with the whispering in exchange for the ability to bind the dead to their service.

In life they performed their arts in secret, raising corpses none would miss, or binding ghosts no one even knew were haunting them. Yet in death, that’s where their true power lay.

With their souls withered away and consumed by the dread Imaru, the necromancers were no longer limited by the last vestiges of morality, and with the new powers at their command, turned a struggling defence against the undead, into a horror-filled nightmare where each fallen ally would rise as a foe.

{{Journal entry|
Saradominist mages preferred the hefty swing of an oak staff over the more pliable ash. They felt that sturdier oak allowed for more powerful spells. The more durable wood was less prone to shattering itself into splinters when they cast their most devastating magic. 

While most wizards practised familiar spells, pushing their research into different practical applications for what was already known, one wizard would push the boundaries of spellcasting. Her name was Cynthia Valtis, and she would go down in local legend.

She would have liked to be remembered for her ability to transform twigs into carrots, thus preventing the famine that threatened Brynmoor. She would have wanted to be remembered for her clever application of wind and water magic to create a nice cool breeze during the summer heat. But, alas, she would be remembered for an ill-advised fire magic experiment that would see her travel across the continent faster than any wizard before. 

Her body has yet to be found. 
}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
The longbow is every hunter’s friend. Capable of taking down prey over a greater range than the shortbow, it has been the end of many a deer trying to flee through the woods. 

Bramblemead would host a thrilling archery tournament. The villagers would proudly bring their own longbows, meticulously crafted by hand, and compete to take down cleverly hidden targets scattered across the village. It was a spectacle of skill and precision, with the only rule being that the target must be shootable from the open street. 

With the introduction of magic, the competition took on a whole new level of silliness. Participants conjured magical air currents that sent arrows astray – often into unsuspecting washing lines or pies cooling on windowsills – or they would playfully blast arrows out of the air with fire spells. 

However, this stopped after the Amalgamated archer, Derien, joined the game. Gifted with the element of air, his arrows curved gracefully with each shot, missing traps, tricks and deceptions. His victory earned the Amalgamated more jealousy, which led to the competition ending out of envious spite.
}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
The villagers who proved their skills with an ash shortbow were brought into the forest by a Wild Knight instructor in search of more durable wood. The oak stood proud and tall in the forest, standing firm against the ebb of time. Villagers would gather the sturdiest branches that they could and be brought to a quiet place in the wood to begin carving their new bows. 

The Wild Knight would tell them that a good bow is more than just a weapon, but an extension of oneself. They encouraged each villager to put a piece of themselves into the bow, a decoration on the handle, or a poem carved into the wood. Whatever made the bow personal to them. 

This connection in the crafting process would help the villagers feel comfortable with their new weapon, and many young hunters would use the same bow throughout their lives. It even became a tradition for young hunters to gift a bow to their beloved as a marriage proposal. A tradition that survived into the third age.
}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
Magic always inspires people. Something about rewriting the underpinning rules of your reality, with little more than force of will and a handful of stones, makes people reach for lofty goals. In Fellhollow it was the wizard Falistrius that wanted to make a name for themselves.

They wanted to be a magical scholar. A researching who might uncover the secrets of the universe itself. They sought spells of greater and greater power, dabbling in mysteries both profane and forbidden, and came up empty handed.

After constantly searching for power, it was an unexpected duel that would grant her the fame she sought, at a price she would have preferred to avoid. A travelling elven sorcerer arrived in the village of Emberwood one night and the local drunk foolishly picked a fight with him. Unfortunately for Falistrius that drunk was her wife.

The elf challenged the drunk to a duel, for satisfaction over a drink spilled, and by local custom Falistrius was forced to answer. They met in the forests of Fellhollow, and unleashed their magic.

The elf’s spells were like nothing she had ever seen before. Cold and dark, sanguine and terrible, they tore into her magical defences like they were nothing and writhed inside her soul like a foul nightmare. Against the strain, her staff shattered, leaving her vulnerable and in desperation she grasped a fallen hollow tree branch and urged her magic through it.

It wasn’t enough to save her. But it was enough to earn the respect and satisfaction of the sorcerer, who left the region with his pale-skinned cohorts. Ever since then, young Fellhollow mages would craft staves from the hollow bark from the forest, in memory of Falistrius.
}}

{{Journal entry|
In the third age, before someone could wield a staff of light, it would first need to be blessed by three people. 

A priest would bless it first, instilling the weapon with Saradomin’s wisdom. A monk would bless it second, imbuing the staff with the humility of Saradomin. Finally, an icyene general would give their blessing, dedicating the weapon to Saradomin’s righteousness. 

Those battlemages chosen to wield such a sacred weapon would dive into battle against Zamorak’s forces and believe themselves invulnerable. 

They were often proved wrong. 

Yet, those who carried the staff into battle seemed to survive longer than their compatriots. The defensive magic of the staff kept them alive longer than others. A demon once stole a staff and tried to use that power for himself. Still, when he tried to channel demonic power through the staff, it is said that the explosion could be seen from across the battlefield.

{{Journal entry|
Power corrupts, and what’s more powerful than an enormous axe comprised of a metal stronger than any seen before? Such was the logic of Olga Skulltaker (not her real name), the self-styled bandit queen of Fellhollow.

As a child, Olga had always enjoyed listening to her grandfather’s stories from the mainland. Tales of mighty warriors defeating terrifying foes. Purehearted heroes challenging evil knights to great battles across pointlessly high bridges and the like. Her parents always laughed and called her “their little hero” but the truth was she was far more interested in the villain.

When she was old enough to wield a weapon, she trained with the biggest axes she could carry, and her sparring partners feared facing off against her because she always took things too far. Once even costing another student their fingers.

As an adult, she found a place for herself among the Children of Shadows. She had hoped they would be dangerous, wicked people, like herself, but instead they spend their time reciting terrible poetry and talking about evil, without ever doing it.

So she took her axe, changed her name, and found the highest bridge she could, and attacked anyone that tried to cross it.
}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
Metal is difficult to mine with inferior tools. A lesson that one dwarf tried very hard not to learn. Baralas, a dwarf from Keldagrim, once refused to trade up his bronze pickaxe for anything else. He was convinced, that any metal could mine any other metal, because what he was targeting was the stone, not the ore itself. An interesting plan, and one with tragic results. 

While mining a rare metal with a particularly solid structure, his pick struck a single piece of the ore, no bigger than a pebble, and his bronze pick shattered into countless pieces as a result. Like an explosion made from tiny little metallic shards, Baralas was shredded into nothing but the lingering stench of regret. 

Now, dwarves make it their business to find the hardest, strongest and most impressive pickaxes out there, lest they become as much a stain on history as Baralas was on the mine's wall. 
}}
