{{Journal entry|
It is said that the origins of the scimitar come from Al Kharid, where skilled swordsmen would wield them in a dazzling manner akin to a dance. Travelling dignitaries would be wowed by the spectacle, applauding great choreographed sword clashes that dramatized legendary battles of history’s past.

They were brought to Ashenfall by a noble family during the god wars, who had taken up the scimitar as their weapon of choice, in service, of course, of the mighty Saradomin. This family was proud and pious, which made them all the more concerned when their daughter was one of the first to show signs of Amalgamation.

Love, for once, triumphed over prejudice, and the family scorned their wealth and prestige in order to protect their child and they joined many others who fled the growing unrest in the village of Bramblemead and travelled north to Fellhollow. There, they taught the secrets of the scimitar to the local blacksmiths, and the weapon found itself a great deal of popularity in the times to come.

His family and friends escaped to the Silverthorn Keep and Lionel waited at the guardhouse, standing as a wall against the tide of the undead. One of the first weapons ever created, the stone dagger has a sinister history. At first it allowed early humans, dwarves, elves and other intelligent species to thrive. They could take down prey and feast on the spoils, using the dagger to pare down the kill, making it easier to eat. It created the gap between animals and people, the first step toward civilization. 

It’s also the first tool to lead to murder. 

A young man whose name has long been forgotten once created a dagger of glittering black stone. Pleased with his work, he proudly displayed it, earning admiration and envy from those around him. 
So proud was he of the dagger that he would whisper to it, acting as though it would whisper back. On the day he slit the chieftain’s throat, he claimed that the dagger had told him to do it. 

Fortunately most stone daggers are pleasingly silent.

Trees are arrogant creatures, standing tall in the forests and refusing to bow to the wind. For decades they spread their roots claiming dominion over the nearby soil. The claws of beasts are a mere distraction. Raging storms barely rustle their leaves. They refuse to move for anyone, arrogant to the core.

Yet, it is not the wind, nor the heavens that shatter their resolve. Indeed, it is the lowliest of stones, refined to an edge. No matter how old the tree, how sturdy its fame, a single stone, the size of your fist, can bring the mightiest ash low.  

The stone axe is an alliance of such a rock, working together with branches cast aside in the tree’s hubris. Proof that even the lowliest of us can make a difference.

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
Ulv was always the silent hunter, in more ways than one. While it was true that no word ever left his lips, his footsteps, breath and, most importantly, his arrows, were all equally devoid of sound. The Wild Knights would jokingly call him the Silent Killer – though over time the crueler members of the order called him the Silent But Deadly, knowing he lacked the capability to argue back. The boy took these insults with quiet grace, never biting back, never reacting. He was used to those little cruelties, having faced them all his life. 

He had carved the bow himself and once walked Ravanna through the process. The two of them were as true a friendship as could ever be hoped for. No lingering romantic tensions. No transaction or debt. No honour chained them together. They were friends simply because they were. Because two lonely people found each other and found a comfort in each others eccentricities. The wolf and the bat, platonic soulmates to the end. 

For one of his birthdays, Ravanna enchanted the bow with a simple spell. She took animal bones, skulls and hides and wove necromantic magic through them, wrapping them around the limbs and grip of the bow, imbuing them with just enough of the underworld to strip them of their sound and a little of their substance. Like ghosts, the arrows would sail silently through the air, dropping targets before they ever knew what hit them. 

It would have been the perfect birthday gift. If only Ulv had lived long enough to receive it. 

The garou can be brutal in their assaults, considering notions like mercy to be the domain of the weak-willed, or the cowardly. Ulv was simply in the wrong place, at the wrong time, and was ambushed by a patrol of young garou, looking for the bloodmark that would grant them adulthood. There were six of them in total, but Ulv reduced them down to four, before the claws entered his throat and silenced him forever. 

When Ravanna found his body, she went mad. An anger unlike any other, a rage more powerful than any storm, waged a war inside her between the light and the dark. The darkness won. Using the souls of slain garou, Ravanna's necromantic curse tore through the Highlands, twisting the clouds into screaming things, filled with a fraction of the rage she felt. As the ghosts of the dead garou crashed about within them, the clouds unleashed lightning and thunder upon the populace below, destroying countless settlements in an instant and countless more over the centuries that followed. 
}}

===Recipe tree===
{{Crafting Tree|Wild Scout's Shortbow}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
There was magic once, in this bow, though it has mostly faded now. Runes were ground down and mixed with plant oils, to create a special resin that allowed the Wild Knights to work their magic through the bow, as if they were carrying runes. That magic has faded away, and the recipe for the mixture lost to the ages, but these bows are still formidable in their own right.

Wild Knights told tales of creatures that lived within the wilds of Ashenfall, that could not be felled by normal bows. Deer with hides that glistened with starlight, sheep who’s silver fleeces repelled all arrows. They claimed that these magically infused bows were the only ones capable of harming the creatures, though none ever returned with trophies to share.
}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
Ulv had many skills, but hunting was his strongest. He was inherently quiet, still as the night, and he could hold his position, in the trees or bushes, for hours at a time. Ravanna was never good at this. When the two of them hunted together, Ravanna would sneeze, cough or scream at the sight of an unexpected insect, and the two of them would watch their quarry disappear off into the night.

Although this would occasionally test their friendship, Ulv never really held it against Ravanna. Instead he continued attempting to teach the necromancer the ways of the forest, and the techniques the Wild Knights would use to track down game. It never took. Try as she might, Ravanna was never going to be silent as a shadow.

In apology, she looked for a way to create a weapon that would reduce the impact of her noisy nature. Longbows fired further and faster, meaning that less stealth was needed. She made her way into Fellhollow in search of a material strong enough, and returned with willow branches that she crafted into a longbow as a gift for her friend.

Their hunts improved dramatically afterward. That was, until they became the hunted.
}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
As the dead rose in greater and greater numbers, the villagers needed stronger weapons to defeat them. Their ash and oak longbows failed to unleash sufficient force needed to stem the relentless tide of the undead. They needed a stronger material, that was also flexible enough to deliver arrows of great enough force.

Willow was their solution. It is said that the first willow shortbow was gifted to a villager by a spirit that dwelled within the grove. Legends say that the spirit had an unnatural beauty, and would lure foolish villagers into the waters where they would be drowned. Yet, somehow, one villager earned not the spirits ire, but their admiration.

The spirit gave up their immortal life, to court the villager. They brought gifts of flowers, fish and finally they gifted a shortbow made from the willow trees in the spirits grove. The validity of this tale is hotly debated, with most assuming it is little more than myth, yet willow groves are still considered spiritual places, where one must be careful who they talk to.
}}

|mat1qty = 14
|output1 = Wooden Training Sword

===Recipe tree===
{{Crafting Tree|Wooden Training Sword}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
In the village of Bramblemead, children grew up knowing battle. The God Wars hadn’t reached them yet, but the priests always knew that the danger was coming. So children were taught combat in the form of a game.

Carpenters were encouraged to make little wooden swords, so that the children could emulate the noble paladins that would wander the village. These soldiers were held up as the peak aspiration, young men and women daydreamed through school, about taking up those glittering swords and running off into adventure.

These weapons clicked and clacked against one another, harmless it seemed to the adults that watched. But wood in Bramblemead was hardened and preserved by druidic magic, and it soon became clear the damage these swords could deal. Injuries were common, bruises and broken bones were the rite of passage of every child.

It was fortunate, perhaps, that these weapons were so painful – because the children of Bramblemead grew up with a better understanding that war was no game.
}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
There are myths and anecdotes about Zamorak appearing to the inhabitants of Dowdun Reach. Few truly believe them. Zamorak is not one for hiding his presence: he's more theatrical than that.

It may be hard to believe, but some have tried to 'summon' Zamorak to Dowdun Reach. Call it the hubris of a demon summoner: a student feels they have mastered the art of summoning demons, so believes the next rung on the ladder is god. Never mind that Zamorak has no ounce of demon within him.

Zamorak can be accused of many things, but he does have a sense of humour. These attempts have been greeted with a gift. He has been known to kick a bloodveld through the portal, or another creature he has to hand. It gives the demon summoner a little spot-test.
}}

===Recipe tree===
{{Crafting Tree|Zombie Axe}}

==Journal==
{{Journal entry|
Captain Artorius Flamhanger was a brave man, who stood against the rampaging forces of the damned even as his defences crumbled around him. He never wavered, never faltered, and he never left a man behind.

In a better world, there would be songs about him. But Fellhollow scorns legacy, leaving only ruin and despair where hope might take root.

He held the line against the encroaching horde far longer than anywhere else in the region. Days turned into months and months grew into years. As the rest of the region vanished into death, despair and rot, Captain Flamhanger stood strong. As his children died and rose again, the captain returned them to the earth with sombre compassion. When his wife joined them in death, he gave her a final kiss of polished silver that cleaved her head from her shoulders.

In a better world he might have held back the darkness, stood as the single ray of light in a world of shadow. But this is not our world.

There are no sagas of this man. No great texts telling of his heroic deeds. The only sound he made in the time after his death, is the bubbling song of digestive acids within a zogre’s belly.

History is penned by the survivors and the victors, yet the deeds of the dead echo across time. This axe, simple as it may appear, is infused with vengeance against the dead that had taken so much from  a good man.
}}
